ثُمَّ قَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿يَعِظُكُمُ اللَّهُ أَنْ تَعُودُوا لِمِثْلِهِ أَبَدًا﴾ أَيْ: يَنْهَاكُمُ اللَّهُ متوعِّدًا أَنْ يَقَعَ مِنْكُمْ مَا يُشْبِهُ هَذَا أَبَدًا، أَيْ: فِيمَا يُسْتَقْبَلُ. فَلِهَذَا قَالَ: ﴿إِنْ كُنْتُمْ مُؤْمِنِينَ﴾ أَيْ: إِنْ كُنْتُمْ تُؤْمِنُونَ بِاللَّهِ وَشَرْعِهِ، وَتُعَظِّمُونَ رَسُولَهُ ﷺ، فَأَمَّا مَنْ كَانَ مُتَّصِفًا بِالْكُفْرِ فَذَاكَ لَهُ حُكْمٌ آخَرُ.

ثُمَّ قَالَ: ﴿وَيُبَيِّنُ اللَّهُ لَكُمُ الآيَاتِ﴾ أَيْ: يُوَضِّحُ لَكُمُ الْأَحْكَامَ الشَّرْعِيَّةَ والحِكَمَ القَدَريّة، ﴿وَاللَّهُ عَلِيمٌ حَكِيمٌ﴾ أَيْ: عَلِيمٌ بِمَا يُصْلِحُ عِبَادَهُ، حَكِيمٌ فِي شَرْعه وقَدَره.

---

## 24:19 — verse 19

### Translation

This is a third form of discipline for one who hears something of bad speech, so that something of it settles in his mind and he speaks it: let him not spread it excessively, circulate it, and broadcast it. For the Almighty has said: {Indeed, those who love that immorality should be spread among those who believe}, meaning: they choose that ugly speech about them should become widespread, {will have a painful punishment in this world}, meaning: through the legal penalty (hadd), {and in the Hereafter}, meaning: through chastisement, {and Allah knows and you do not know}, meaning: so refer matters back to Him and you will be guided rightly.

Imam Ahmad said: Muhammad ibn Bakr told us, Maymun ibn Abi Muhammad al-Mar'i told us, Muhammad ibn Abbad al-Makhzumi told us, from Thawban, from the Prophet ﷺ, who said: "Do not harm the servants of Allah, do not disgrace them, and do not seek out their private faults. For whoever seeks out the private fault of his Muslim brother, Allah will seek out his private fault, until He exposes him in his own house."

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

وَهَذَا تَأْدِيبٌ ثَالِثٌ لِمَنْ سَمِعَ شَيْئًا مِنَ الْكَلَامِ السَّيِّئِ، فَقَامَ بِذِهْنِهِ مِنْهُ شَيْءٌ، وَتَكَلَّمَ بِهِ، فَلَا يُكْثِرُ مِنْهُ وَيُشِيعُهُ وَيُذِيعُهُ، فَقَدْ قَالَ تَعَالَى : ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يُحِبُّونَ أَنْ تَشِيعَ الْفَاحِشَةُ فِي الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا﴾ أَيْ: يَخْتَارُونَ ظُهُورَ الْكَلَامِ عَنْهُمْ بِالْقَبِيحِ، ﴿لَهُمْ عَذَابٌ أَلِيمٌ فِي الدُّنْيَا﴾ أَيْ: بِالْحَدِّ، وَفِي الْآخِرَةِ بِالْعَذَابِ، ﴿وَاللَّهُ يَعْلَمُ وَأَنْتُمْ لَا تَعْلَمُونَ﴾ أَيْ: فَرُدُّوا الْأُمُورَ إِلَيْهِ تَرْشُدُوا.

وَقَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ بَكْرٍ، حَدَّثَنَا مَيْمُونُ بْنُ أَبِي مُحَمَّدٍ المَرَئيّ، حَدَّثَنَا مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ عَبّاد الْمَخْزُومِيُّ، عَنْ ثَوْبَان، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ قَالَ: "لَا تُؤذوا عِبادَ اللَّهِ وَلَا تُعيِّروهم، ولا تطلبوا عَوَرَاتِهِمْ، فَإِنَّهُ مَنْ طَلَبَ عَوْرَةَ أَخِيهِ الْمُسْلِمِ، طَلَبَ اللَّهُ عَوْرَتَهُ، حَتَّى يَفْضَحَهُ فِي بَيْتِهِ" .

---

## 24:20-21 — verses 20-21 (shared commentary)

### Translation

The Exalted says: {And were it not for the favor of Allah upon you and His mercy, and that Allah is Compassionate and Merciful}, meaning: were it not for this, the matter would have been otherwise, but He, the Exalted, is Compassionate toward His servants and Merciful to them. So He accepted the repentance of whoever repented to Him regarding this [matter], and purified whoever among them was purified through the prescribed punishment that was carried out upon him.

Then He said: {O you who believe, do not follow the footsteps of Satan}, meaning: his paths and ways and what he commands. {And whoever follows the footsteps of Satan, indeed he commands indecency and wrongdoing}: this is a warning and a cautioning against that, in the most eloquent, concise, powerful and excellent expression.

Ali ibn Abi Talha reported from Ibn Abbas: "the footsteps of Satan" means his work. Ikrimah said: his promptings. Qatadah said: every sin is among the footsteps of Satan. Abu Mijlaz said: vows made regarding acts of disobedience are among the footsteps of Satan.

Masruq said: a man asked Ibn Mas'ud, saying, "I have made it forbidden for myself to eat food." He replied: "This is among the promptings of Satan. Make expiation for your oath, and eat."

Al-Sha'bi said regarding a man who had vowed to slaughter his son: "This is among the promptings of Satan," and he gave the ruling that he should instead slaughter a ram.

Ibn Abi Hatim said: [chain] Abu Rafi' said: my wife became angry with me and said: "She [meaning herself] shall be a Jewess one day and a Christian the next, and every slave she owns shall be free, if you do not divorce your wife." So I went to Abdullah ibn Umar, and he said: "This is only among the promptings of Satan." Zaynab bint Umm Salamah, who at that time was the most learned woman in Medina in matters of jurisprudence, said the same. And I went to Asim ibn Umar, and he said the same thing.

Then the Exalted said: {And were it not for the favor of Allah upon you and His mercy, not one of you would ever have been purified}, meaning: were it not that He grants repentance and a return to Him to whomever He wills, and purifies souls from their associating partners with Him, their immorality, their corruption, and whatever evil traits are in them, each according to its measure, no one would have attained any purification or good for himself. {But Allah purifies whomever He wills}, meaning: among His creation, and He leads astray whomever He wills and casts him down into the destructive pits of misguidance and error.

And His saying: {And Allah is All-Hearing}, meaning: hearing the words of His servants, {All-Knowing} of them, knowing who among them deserves guidance and who deserves misguidance.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يَقُولُ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَلَوْلا فَضْلُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَتُهُ وَأَنَّ اللَّهَ رَءُوفٌ رَحِيمٌ﴾ أَيْ: لَوْلَا هَذَا لَكَانَ أَمْرٌ آخَرُ، وَلَكِنَّهُ تَعَالَى رُؤُوفٌ بِعِبَادِهِ، رَحِيمٌ بِهِمْ. فَتَابَ عَلَى مَنْ تَابَ إِلَيْهِ مِنْ هَذِهِ [الْقَضِيَّةِ] وطَهَّر مَنْ طَهَّر مِنْهُمْ بِالْحَدِّ الَّذِي أُقِيمَ عَلَيْهِ.

ثُمَّ قَالَ: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لَا تَتَّبِعُوا خُطُوَاتِ الشَّيْطَانِ﴾ يَعْنِي: طَرَائِقَهُ وَمَسَالِكَهُ وَمَا يَأْمُرُ بِهِ، ﴿وَمَنْ يَتَّبِعْ خُطُوَاتِ الشَّيْطَانِ فَإِنَّهُ يَأْمُرُ بِالْفَحْشَاءِ وَالْمُنْكَرِ﴾ : هَذَا تَنْفِيرٌ وَتَحْذِيرٌ مِنْ ذَلِكَ، بِأَفْصَحِ الْعِبَارَةِ وَأَوْجَزِهَا وَأَبْلَغِهَا وَأَحْسَنِهَا.

قَالَ عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَلْحَةَ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿خُطُوَاتِ الشَّيْطَانِ﴾ : عَمَلَهُ. وَقَالَ عِكْرِمَةُ: نَزَغَاتِهِ. وَقَالَ قَتَادَةُ: كُلُّ مَعْصِيَةٍ فَهِيَ مِنْ خُطُوَاتِ الشَّيْطَانِ. وَقَالَ أَبُو مِجْلَز: النُّذُورُ فِي الْمَعَاصِي مِنْ خُطُوَاتِ الشَّيْطَانِ.

وَقَالَ مَسْرُوقٌ: سَأَلَ رَجُلٌ ابْنَ مَسْعُودٍ فَقَالَ: إِنِّي حَرَّمْتُ أَنْ آكُلَ طَعَامًا؟ فَقَالَ: هَذَا مِنْ نَزَعَاتِ الشَّيْطَانِ، كَفِّر عَنْ يَمِينِكَ، وكُل.

وَقَالَ الشَّعْبِيُّ فِي رَجُلٍ نَذَر ذَبْح وَلَدِهِ: هَذَا مِنْ نَزَغَاتِ الشَّيْطَانِ، وَأَفْتَاهُ أَنْ يَذْبَحَ كَبْشًا.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبِي، حَدَّثَنَا حَسَّانُ بْنُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ الْمِصْرِيُّ، حَدَّثَنَا السَّرِيُّ بْنُ يَحْيَى، عَنْ سُلَيْمَانَ التَّيْمِيِّ، عَنْ أَبِي رَافِعٍ قَالَ: غَضِبْتُ عليَّ امْرَأَتِي فَقَالَتْ: هِيَ يَوْمًا يَهُودِيَّةٌ، وَيَوْمًا نَصْرَانِيَّةٌ، وَكُلُّ مَمْلُوكٍ لَهَا حُرٌّ، إِنْ لَمْ تُطْلِّقِ امْرَأَتَكَ. فَأَتَيْتُ عَبْدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ عُمَرَ فَقَالَ: إِنَّمَا هَذِهِ مِنْ نَزَغَاتِ الشَّيْطَانِ. وَكَذَلِكَ قَالَتْ زَيْنَبُ بِنْتُ أُمِّ سَلَمَةَ، وَهِيَ يَوْمَئِذٍ أَفْقَهُ امْرَأَةٍ بِالْمَدِينَةِ، وَأَتَيْتُ عَاصِمَ بْنَ عُمَرَ، فَقَالَ مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ.

ثُمَّ قَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَلَوْلا فَضْلُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَتُهُ مَا زَكَا مِنْكُمْ مِنْ أَحَدٍ أَبَدًا﴾ أَيْ: لَوْلَا هُوَ يَرْزُقُ مَنْ يَشَاءُ التَّوْبَةَ وَالرُّجُوعَ إِلَيْهِ، وَيُزَكِّي النُّفُوسَ مِنْ شِرْكِهَا وَفُجُورِهَا وَدَسِّهَا وَمَا فِيهَا مِنْ أَخْلَاقٍ رَدِيئَةٍ، كُلٌّ بِحَسَبِهِ، لَمَا حَصَّلَ أَحَدٌ لِنَفْسِهِ زَكَاةً وَلَا خَيْرًا ﴿وَلَكِنَّ اللَّهَ يُزَكِّي مَنْ يَشَاءُ﴾ أَيْ: مَنْ خَلْقِهِ، وَيُضِلُّ مَنْ يَشَاءُ وَيُرْدِيهِ فِي مَهَالِكِ الضَّلَالِ وَالْغَيِّ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَاللَّهُ سَمِيعٌ﴾ أَيْ: سَمِيعٌ لِأَقْوَالِ عِبَادِهِ ﴿عَلِيمٌ﴾ بِهَمْ، مَنْ يَسْتَحِقُّ مِنْهُمُ الْهُدَى وَالضَّلَالَ.

---

## 24:22 — verse 22

### Translation

The Exalted says: {And let not swear} from al-alliyyah, [which is: the oath], meaning: let them not swear, {those of you who possess bounty}, meaning wealth, generosity and beneficence, {and abundance}, meaning affluence, {that they will not give to those near of kin, and the needy, and those who migrated in the way of Allah}, meaning: do not swear that you will not maintain ties with your relatives among the poor and the migrants. This is at the utmost degree of gentleness and compassion regarding the maintenance of family ties. For this reason He said: {and let them pardon and let them overlook}, meaning: regarding the wrong and harm that had preceded from them. This is part of His forbearance, generosity and kindness toward His creation, despite their wronging of themselves.

This verse was revealed concerning al-Siddiq, when he swore that he would never again do any good to Mistah ibn Uthathah, after Mistah had said what he said about A'ishah, as was mentioned previously in the hadith. When Allah revealed the declaration of innocence of the Mother of the Believers, A'ishah, and the believing hearts became at ease and settled, and Allah accepted the repentance of those among the believers who had spoken of that matter, and the prescribed punishment (hadd) was carried out upon whoever it was carried out upon, then Allah, Blessed and Exalted, to whom belongs all bounty and favor, ordained that al-Siddiq should turn again in kindness toward his relative and kinsman, namely Mistah ibn Uthathah. For Mistah was the son of al-Siddiq's maternal aunt, and he was poor, having no wealth except what Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him, spent on him. He was one of those who had migrated in the way of Allah, and he had uttered a slanderous falsehood (walaqa walqatan), for which Allah accepted his repentance and upon which the prescribed punishment was carried out. Al-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him, was known for doing good, possessing bounty and generous favors toward both relatives and strangers alike. So when this verse was revealed, down to His saying: {Do you not love that Allah should forgive you? And Allah is Forgiving, Merciful}, meaning: the reward corresponds to the deed in kind. Just as you forgive the one who has wronged you, so We will forgive you, and just as you overlook, so We will overlook concerning you. At that, al-Siddiq said: "Yes indeed, by Allah, we do love, O our Lord, that You should forgive us." Then he restored to Mistah the support he used to give him, and said: "By Allah, I will never withdraw it from him again," in contrast to what he had said before: "By Allah, I will never again do him any good." It was for this reason that al-Siddiq was truly al-Siddiq [may Allah be pleased with him and with his daughter].

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يَقُولُ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَلا يَأْتَلِ﴾ مِنَ الأليَّة، [وَهِيَ: الْحَلِفُ] أَيْ: لَا يَحْلِفْ ﴿أُولُو الْفَضْلِ مِنْكُمْ﴾ أَيِ: الطَّول وَالصَّدَقَةِ وَالْإِحْسَانِ ﴿وَالسَّعَة﴾ أَيِ: الجِدَةَ ﴿أَنْ يُؤْتُوا أُولِي الْقُرْبَى وَالْمَسَاكِينَ وَالْمُهَاجِرِينَ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ﴾ أَيْ: لَا تَحْلِفُوا أَلَّا تَصِلُوا قَرَابَاتِكُمُ الْمَسَاكِينَ وَالْمُهَاجِرِينَ. وَهَذِهِ فِي غَايَةِ التَّرَفُّقِ وَالْعَطْفِ عَلَى صِلَةِ الْأَرْحَامِ؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ: ﴿وَلْيَعْفُوا وَلْيَصْفَحُوا﴾ أَيْ: عَمَّا تَقَدَّمَ مِنْهُمْ مِنَ الْإِسَاءَةِ وَالْأَذَى، وَهَذَا مِنْ حِلْمِهِ تَعَالَى وَكَرَمِهِ وَلُطْفِهِ بِخَلْقِهِ مَعَ ظُلْمِهِمْ لِأَنْفُسِهِمْ.

وَهَذِهِ الْآيَةُ نَزَلَتْ فِي الصدِّيق، حِينَ حَلَفَ أَلَّا يَنْفَعَ مِسْطَح بْنَ أُثَاثَةَ بِنَافِعَةٍ بَعْدَمَا قَالَ فِي عَائِشَةَ مَا قَالَ، كَمَا تَقَدَّمَ فِي الْحَدِيثِ. فَلَمَّا أَنْزَلَ اللَّهُ براءةَ أُمِّ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ عَائِشَةَ، وَطَابَتِ النُّفُوسُ الْمُؤْمِنَةُ وَاسْتَقَرَّتْ، وَتَابَ اللَّهُ عَلَى مَن كَانَ تَكَلَّمَ مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ فِي ذَلِكَ، وَأُقِيمَ الْحَدُّ عَلَى مَن أُقِيمَ عَلَيْهِ -شَرَع تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى، وَلَهُ الْفَضْلُ وَالْمِنَّةُ، يعطفُ الصدِّيق عَلَى قَرِيبِهِ وَنَسِيبِهِ، وَهُوَ مِسْطَح بْنُ أُثَاثَةَ، فَإِنَّهُ كَانَ ابْنَ خَالَةِ الصَّدِيقِ، وَكَانَ مِسْكِينًا لَا مَالَ لَهُ إِلَّا مَا يُنْفِقُ عَلَيْهِ أَبُو بَكْرٍ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، وَكَانَ مِنَ الْمُهَاجِرِينَ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ، وَقَدْ وَلَق وَلْقَة تَابَ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ مِنْهَا، وضُرب الْحَدَّ عَلَيْهَا. وَكَانَ الصَّدِّيقُ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، مَعْرُوفًا بِالْمَعْرُوفِ، لَهُ الْفَضْلُ وَالْأَيَادِي عَلَى الْأَقَارِبِ وَالْأَجَانِبِ. فَلَمَّا نَزَلَتْ هَذِهِ الْآيَةُ إِلَى قَوْلِهِ: ﴿أَلا تُحِبُّونَ أَنْ يَغْفِرَ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ وَاللَّهُ غَفُورٌ رَحِيمٌ﴾ أَيْ: فَإِنَّ الْجَزَاءَ مِنْ جِنْسِ الْعَمَلِ، فَكَمَا تَغْفِرُ عَنِ الْمُذْنِبِ إِلَيْكَ نَغْفِرُ لَكَ، وَكَمَا تَصْفَحُ نَصْفَحُ عَنْكَ. فَعِنْدَ ذَلِكَ قَالَ الصَّدِّيقُ: بَلَى، وَاللَّهِ إِنَّا نُحِبُّ -يَا رَبَّنَا -أَنْ تَغْفِرَ لَنَا. ثُمَّ رَجَع إِلَى مِسْطَحٍ مَا كَانَ يَصِلُهُ مِنَ النَّفَقَةِ، وَقَالَ: وَاللَّهِ لَا أَنْزَعُهَا مِنْهُ أَبَدًا، فِي مُقَابَلَةِ مَا كَانَ قَالَ: وَاللَّهِ لَا أَنْفَعُهُ بِنَافِعَةٍ أَبَدًا، فَلِهَذَا كَانَ الصِّدِّيقُ هُوَ الصَّدِّيقُ [رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ وَعَنْ بِنْتِهِ] .

---

## 24:23-25 — verses 23-25 (shared commentary)

### Translation

This is a threat from Allah, exalted is He, against those who accuse the chaste, heedless, believing women, expressed in the dominant form.

The Mothers of the Believers are more entitled to be included in this than any other chaste woman, especially the one who was the occasion of the revelation, namely Aisha bint al-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with them both.

The scholars, may Allah have mercy on them, are unanimously agreed that whoever reviles her after this and accuses her of what she was accused of, after what has been mentioned in this verse, is a disbeliever, because he is opposing the Qur'an in obstinance. Regarding the rest of the Mothers of the Believers there are two opinions, the more correct of which is that they are like her, and Allah knows best.

Concerning His saying, exalted is He, {they are cursed in this world and the next, and for them is a mighty punishment}, this is like His saying: {Indeed, those who annoy Allah and His Messenger, Allah has cursed them in this world and the next, and has prepared for them a humiliating punishment} [al-Ahzab: 57].

Some have held that this is specific to Aisha. Ibn Abi Hatim said:

[chain] Ibn Abbas said regarding {Indeed, those who accuse the chaste, heedless, believing women}: it was revealed specifically about Aisha.

Sa'id ibn Jubayr and Muqatil ibn Hayyan said likewise. Ibn Jarir mentioned it from Aisha herself, saying:

[chain] Aisha said: I was accused of what I was accused of while I was heedless of it, and it reached me only afterward. She said: While the Messenger of Allah ﷺ was sitting with me, revelation came to him. She said: When revelation came to him, it would take hold of him like a state of drowsiness. Revelation came to him while he was sitting with me, then he sat up straight, wiping his face, and said: "O Aisha, rejoice." I said: By the praise of Allah, not by your praise. Then he recited {Indeed, those who accuse the chaste, heedless, believing women} up to {those are declared innocent of what they say} [al-Nur: 26].

This is how it is related, but it does not state that the ruling is specific to her. It only indicates that she was the occasion of the revelation, distinct from others, even though the ruling applies to her as it applies to others. This is perhaps what Ibn Abbas and those who said the same meant, and Allah knows best.

Al-Dahhak, Abu al-Jawza, and Salamah ibn Nubayt said: what is meant by it are the wives of the Prophet specifically, excluding other women.

Al-Awfi reported from Ibn Abbas concerning His saying {Indeed, those who accuse the chaste, heedless, believing women}, the verse: meaning the wives of the Prophet ﷺ, whom the hypocrites accused, so Allah decreed for them the curse and wrath, and they incurred the displeasure of Allah. This was concerning the wives of the Prophet ﷺ. Then afterward was revealed {And those who accuse chaste women and then do not bring four witnesses} up to His saying {then indeed Allah is forgiving, merciful}. So Allah revealed the flogging and the acceptance of repentance: repentance is accepted, but testimony is rejected.

Ibn Jarir said: [chain] a shaykh from Banu Asad, from Ibn Abbas, said: he explained Surat al-Nur, and when he reached this verse, {Indeed, those who accuse the chaste, heedless, believing women are cursed}, the verse, he said: it concerns the matter of Aisha and the wives of the Prophet ﷺ, and it is unspecified, and there is no repentance for them. Then he recited {And those who accuse chaste women and then do not bring four witnesses} up to His saying {except those who repent after that and reform}, the verse [al-Nur: 4-5]. He said: so He granted repentance to those, but did not grant repentance to those who accused these women. He said: some of the people present were about to stand and kiss his head, because of the excellence of his explanation of Surat al-Nur.

His statement "it is unspecified" means: it is general, covering the prohibition of accusing every chaste woman, and her being cursed in this world and the next.

Similarly Abd al-Rahman ibn Zayd ibn Aslam said: this concerns Aisha, and whoever does likewise today regarding Muslim women, upon him falls what Allah, mighty and majestic, has said, but Aisha was the foremost example of this.

Ibn Jarir preferred the generality of the ruling, and this is correct. Supporting this generality is what Ibn Abi Hatim related:

[chain] Abu Hurayrah reported that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Avoid the seven destructive sins." It was said: O Messenger of Allah, what are they? He said: "Associating partners with Allah, sorcery, killing a soul which Allah has forbidden except by right, consuming usury, consuming the property of an orphan, fleeing on the day of battle, and accusing chaste, heedless, believing women."

Both of them [al-Bukhari and Muslim] related it in the two Sahihs, from the hadith of Sulayman ibn Bilal, with this chain.

Al-Hafiz Abu al-Qasim al-Tabarani said: [chain] Hudhayfah reported from the Prophet ﷺ that he said: "Accusing a chaste woman destroys the deeds of a hundred years."

Concerning His saying {On the day when their tongues, hands, and feet will testify against them regarding what they used to do}, Ibn Abi Hatim said:

[chain] Ibn Abbas said: they, meaning the polytheists, when they see that no one enters Paradise except the people of prayer, will say: come, let us deny it. So they deny it, and Allah seals their mouths, and their hands and feet testify, and they cannot conceal anything from Allah.

Ibn Jarir and Ibn Abi Hatim also said: [chain] the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "When the Day of Resurrection comes, the disbeliever will be recognized by his deeds, and he will deny and dispute. It will be said to him: these are your neighbors, testifying against you. He will say: they lie. Then it will be said: your family and your clan. He will say: they lie. Then it will be said: swear an oath. So they swear, then Allah silences them, and their hands and tongues testify against them, then He casts them into the Fire."

Ibn Abi Hatim also said: [chain] Anas ibn Malik said: We were with the Prophet ﷺ, and he laughed until his molars showed, then he said: "Do you know why I am laughing?" We said: Allah and His Messenger know best. He said: "At the servant's disputation with his Lord on the Day of Resurrection. He will say: O my Lord, did You not protect me from injustice? He will say: Yes indeed. He will say: Then I will not accept any witness against me except from myself. He will say: Your own self suffices today as a witness against you, and the noble recording angels as witnesses. Then his mouth will be sealed, and it will be said to his limbs: speak. So they will speak of his deeds. Then he will be left free to speak, and he will say: away with you, and destruction, for it was on your behalf that I was contending."

Muslim and al-Nasa'i both related it, [chain]. Then al-Nasa'i said: I do not know of anyone who related this hadith from Sufyan al-Thawri other than al-Ashja'i, and it is a gharib (singular) hadith, and Allah knows best. This is what he said.

Qatadah said: O son of Adam, by Allah, upon you are witnesses from your own body that cannot be accused of falsehood, so watch over them and fear Allah in private and in public, for nothing hidden is hidden from Him. Darkness before Him is as light, and the secret before Him is as the open. So whoever is able to die while having good expectation of Allah, let him do so, and there is no strength except by Allah.

Concerning His saying {On that day Allah will pay them in full their true recompense}, Ibn Abbas said: {their recompense} means their reckoning, and everywhere in the Qur'an {their din} means their reckoning. Others said likewise.

As for the reading, the majority read {al-haqq} in the accusative, as a description of "their recompense." Mujahid read it in the nominative, as a description of the Majestic Name. Some of the early generations read it, in the mushaf of Ubayy ibn Ka'b: "On that day Allah, the Truth, will pay them their recompense in full."

Concerning His saying {and they will know that Allah is the manifest Truth}, meaning: His promise, His threat, and His reckoning are the justice in which there is no wrong.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

هَذَا وَعِيدٌ مِنَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى لِلَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَاتِ الْغَافِلَاتِ -خُرِّج مَخْرَجَ الْغَالِبِ -الْمُؤْمِنَاتِ.

فَأُمَّهَاتُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ أَوْلَى بِالدُّخُولِ فِي هَذَا مِنْ كُلِّ مُحَصَّنَةٍ، وَلَا سِيَّمَا الَّتِي كَانَتْ سَبَبَ النُّزُولِ، وَهِيَ عَائِشَةُ بِنْتُ الصَّدِّيقِ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا.

وَقَدْ أَجْمَعَ الْعُلَمَاءُ، رَحِمَهُمُ اللَّهُ، قَاطِبَةً عَلَى أَنَّ مَنْ سَبَّها بَعْدَ هَذَا وَرَمَاهَا بِمَا رَمَاهَا بِهِ [بَعْدَ هذا الَّذِي ذُكِرَ] فِي هَذِهِ الْآيَةِ، فَإِنَّهُ كَافِرٌ؛ لِأَنَّهُ مُعَانِدٌ لِلْقُرْآنِ. وَفِي بَقِيَّةِ أُمَّهَاتِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ قَوْلَانِ: أَصَحُّهُمَا أَنَّهُنَّ كَهِيَ، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: ﴿لُعِنُوا فِي الدُّنْيَا وَالآخِرَةِ وَلَهُمْ عَذَابٌ عَظِيمٌ﴾ كَقَوْلِهِ: ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يُؤْذُونَ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ لَعَنَهُمُ اللَّهُ فِي الدُّنْيَا وَالآخِرَةِ وَأَعَدَّ لَهُمْ عَذَابًا مُهِينًا﴾ [الْأَحْزَابُ: ٥٧] .

وَقَدْ ذَهَبَ بَعْضُهُمْ إِلَى أَنَّهَا خَاصَّةٌ بِعَائِشَةَ، فَقَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ:

حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو سَعِيدٍ الْأَشَجُّ، حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ خِرَاش، عَنِ العَوَّام، عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَيْرٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَاتِ الْغَافِلاتِ الْمُؤْمِنَاتِ﴾ [قَالَ] : نَزَلَتْ فِي عَائِشَةَ خَاصَّةً.

وَكَذَا قَالَ [سَعِيدُ بْنُ جُبَيْرٍ وَ] مُقَاتِلُ بْنُ حَيَّانَ، وَقَدْ ذَكَرَهُ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ فَقَالَ:

حَدَّثَنَا أَحْمَدُ بْنُ عَبْدَة الضَّبِّي، حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو عَوَانة، عَنْ عُمَرَ بْنِ أَبِي سَلَمَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ قَالَ: قَالَتْ عَائِشَةُ: رُميت بِمَا رُمِيتُ بِهِ وَأَنَا غَافِلَةٌ، فَبَلَغَنِي بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ. قَالَتْ: فَبَيْنَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ جَالِسٌ عِنْدِي إِذْ أُوحِيَ، إِلَيْهِ. قَالَتْ: وَكَانَ إِذَا أُوحِيَ إِلَيْهِ أَخَذَهُ كَهَيْئَةِ السُّبات، وَإِنَّهُ أُوحِيَ إِلَيْهِ وَهُوَ جَالِسٌ عِنْدِي، ثُمَّ اسْتَوَى جَالِسًا يَمْسَحُ عَلَى وَجْهِهِ، وَقَالَ: "يَا عَائِشَةُ أَبْشِرِي". قَالَتْ: قُلْتُ: بِحَمْدِ اللَّهِ لَا بِحَمْدِكَ. فَقَرَأَ: ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَاتِ الْغَافِلاتِ الْمُؤْمِنَاتِ﴾ ، حَتَّى قَرَأَ: ﴿أُولَئِكَ مُبَرَّءُونَ مِمَّا يَقُولُونَ﴾ [النُّورِ: ٢٦] .

هَكَذَا أَوْرَدَهُ، وَلَيْسَ فِيهِ أَنَّ الْحُكْمَ خَاصٌّ بِهَا، وَإِنَّمَا فِيهِ أَنَّهَا سَبَبُ النُّزُولِ دُونَ غَيْرِهَا، وَإِنْ كَانَ الْحُكْمُ يَعُمُّهَا كَغَيْرِهَا، وَلَعَلَّهُ مُرَادُ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ وَمَنْ قَالَ كَقَوْلِهِ، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

وَقَالَ الضَّحَّاكُ، وَأَبُو الْجَوْزَاءِ، وَسَلَمَةُ بْنُ نُبَيْط: الْمُرَادُ بِهَا أَزْوَاجُ النَّبِيِّ خَاصَّةً، دُونَ غَيْرِهِنَّ مِنَ النِّسَاءِ.

وَقَالَ العَوْفِيّ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَاتِ الْغَافِلاتِ الْمُؤْمِنَاتِ﴾ الْآيَةَ: يَعْنِي أَزْوَاجَ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ، رَمَاهُنَّ أَهْلُ النِّفَاقِ، فَأَوْجَبَ اللَّهُ لَهُمُ اللَّعْنَةَ وَالْغَضَبَ، وَبَاؤُوا بِسَخَطٍ مِنَ اللَّهِ، فَكَانَ ذَلِكَ فِي أَزْوَاجِ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ ثُمَّ نَزَلَ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَاتِ ثُمَّ لَمْ يَأْتُوا بِأَرْبَعَةِ شُهَدَاءَ﴾ إِلَى قَوْلِهِ: ﴿فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ غَفُورٌ رَحِيمٌ﴾ ، فَأَنْزَلَ اللَّهُ الْجَلْدَ وَالتَّوْبَةَ، فَالتَّوْبَةُ تُقْبَلُ، وَالشَّهَادَةُ تُرَدّ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنَا الْقَاسِمُ، حَدَّثَنَا الْحُسَيْنُ، حَدَّثَنَا هُشَيْم، أَخْبَرَنَا الْعَوَّامُ بْنُ حَوُشَبٍ، عَنْ شَيْخٍ مَنْ بَنِي أَسَدٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ -قَالَ: فَسَّرَ سُورَةَ النُّورِ، فَلَمَّا أَتَى عَلَى هَذِهِ الْآيَةِ: ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَاتِ الْغَافِلاتِ الْمُؤْمِنَاتِ لُعِنُوا﴾ الْآيَةَ -قَالَ: فِي شَأْنِ عَائِشَةَ، وَأَزْوَاجِ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ، وَهِيَ مُبْهَمَةٌ، وَلَيْسَتْ لَهُمْ تَوْبَةٌ، ثُمَّ قَرَأَ: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَاتِ ثُمَّ لَمْ يَأْتُوا بِأَرْبَعَةِ شُهَدَاءَ﴾ إِلَى قَوْلِهِ: ﴿إِلا الَّذِينَ تَابُوا مِنْ بَعْدِ ذَلِكَ وَأَصْلَحُوا﴾ الْآيَةَ [النور: ٤، ٥] ، قال: فجعل لِهَؤُلَاءِ تَوْبَةً وَلَمْ يَجْعَلْ لِمَنْ قَذَفَ أُولَئِكَ تَوْبَةً، قَالَ: فَهَمَّ بعضُ الْقَوْمِ أَنْ يَقُومَ إِلَيْهِ فَيُقَبِّلَ رَأْسَهُ، مِنْ حُسْنِ مَا فسَّر بِهِ سُورَةَ النُّورِ .

فَقَوْلُهُ: "وَهِيَ مُبْهَمَةٌ"، أَيْ: عَامَّةٌ فِي تَحْرِيمِ قَذْفِ كُلِّ مُحْصَنَةٍ، ولَعْنته فِي الدُّنْيَا وَالْآخِرَةِ.

وَهَكَذَا قَالَ عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ زَيْدِ بْنِ أَسْلَمَ: هَذَا فِي عَائِشَةَ، وَمَنْ صَنَعَ مِثْلَ هَذَا أَيْضًا الْيَوْمَ فِي الْمُسْلِمَاتِ، فَلَهُ مَا قَالَ اللَّهُ، عَزَّ وَجَلَّ، وَلَكِنْ عَائِشَةُ كَانَتْ إمامَ ذَلِكَ.

وَقَدِ اخْتَارَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ عُمُومَهَا، وَهُوَ الصَّحِيحُ، وَيُعَضِّدُ الْعُمُومَ مَا رَوَاهُ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ:

حَدَّثَنَا أَحْمَدُ بْنُ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ -ابْنُ أَخِي ابْنِ وَهْبٍ -حَدَّثَنَا عَمِّي، حَدَّثَنَا سُلَيْمَانَ بْنِ بِلَالٍ، عَنْ ثَوْرِ بْنِ زَيْدٍ، عَنْ أَبِي الغَيث عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ؛ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ قَالَ: "اجْتَنِبُوا السَّبْعَ الْمُوبِقَاتِ". قِيلَ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، وَمَا هُنَّ؟ قَالَ: "الشِّرْكُ بِاللَّهِ، وَالسِّحْرُ، وَقَتْلُ النَّفْسِ الَّتِي حَرَّمَ اللَّهُ إِلَّا بِالْحَقِّ، وَأَكْلُ الرِّبَا، وَأَكْلُ مَالِ الْيَتِيمِ، وَالتَّوَلِّي يَوْمَ الزَّحْفِ، وَقَذْفُ الْمُحْصَنَاتِ الْغَافِلَاتِ الْمُؤْمِنَاتِ".

أَخْرَجَاهُ فِي الصَّحِيحَيْنِ، مِنْ حَدِيثِ سُلَيْمَانَ بْنِ بِلَالٍ، بِهِ .

وَقَالَ الْحَافِظُ أَبُو الْقَاسِمِ الطَّبَرَانِيُّ: حَدَّثَنَا مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ عَمْرو بْنِ خَالِدٍ الحَذَّاء الْحَرَّانِيُّ، حَدَّثَنِي أَبِي، (ح) وَحَدَّثَنَا أَبُو شُعَيب الْحَرَّانَيُّ، حَدَّثَنَا جَدِّي أَحْمَدُ بْنُ أَبِي شُعَيب، حَدَّثَنَا مُوسَى بْنُ أَعْيَنَ، عَنْ لَيْثٍ، عَنْ أَبِي إِسْحَاقَ، عَنْ صِلَة بْنِ زُفَر، عَنْ حُذَيْفَةَ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ قَالَ:"قَذْفُ الْمُحْصَنَةِ يَهْدِمُ عَمَلَ مِائَةِ سَنَةٍ" .

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ ﴿يَوْمَ تَشْهَدُ عَلَيْهِمْ أَلْسِنَتُهُمْ وَأَيْدِيهِمْ وَأَرْجُلُهُمْ بِمَا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ﴾ قَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ:

حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو سَعِيدٍ الأشَجّ، حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو يَحْيَى الرَّازِيُّ، عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ أَبِي قَيْسٍ، عَنْ مُطَرِّف، عَنِ المِنْهَال، عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَيْرٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: إِنَّهُمْ -يَعْنِي: الْمُشْرِكِينَ -إِذَا رَأوا أَنَّهُ لَا يدخلُ الجنةَ إِلَّا أَهْلُ الصَّلَاةِ، قَالُوا: تَعَالَوْا حَتَّى نَجْحَدَ. فَيَجْحَدُونَ فَيَخْتِمُ [اللَّهُ] عَلَى أَفْوَاهِهِمْ، وَتَشْهَدُ أَيْدِيهِمْ وَأَرْجُلُهُمْ، وَلَا يَكْتُمُونَ اللَّهَ حَدِيثًا.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ، وَابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ أَيْضًا: حَدَّثَنَا يُونُسُ بْنُ عَبْدِ الْأَعْلَى، حَدَّثَنَا ابْنُ وَهْبٍ، أَخْبَرَنِي عَمْرُو بْنُ الْحَارِثِ، عَنْ دَرَّاج، عَنْ أَبِي الْهَيْثَمِ، عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ، عَنْ رسول الله صلى عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ:"إِذَا كَانَ يَوْمُ الْقِيَامَةِ، عُرف الْكَافِرُ بِعَمَلِهِ، فَيَجْحَدُ وَيُخَاصِمُ، فَيُقَالُ لَهُ: هَؤُلَاءِ جِيرَانُكَ يَشْهَدُونَ عَلَيْكَ. فَيَقُولُ: كَذَبُوا. فَيَقُولُ: أَهْلُكَ وَعَشِيرَتُكَ. فَيَقُولُ: كَذَبُوا، فَيَقُولُ: احْلِفُوا. فَيَحْلِفُونَ، ثُمَّ يُصمِتهم اللَّهُ، فَتَشْهَدُ عَلَيْهِمْ أَيْدِيهِمْ وَأَلْسِنَتُهُمْ، ثُمَّ يُدْخِلُهُمُ النَّارَ" .

وَقَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ أَيْضًا: حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو شَيْبَةَ إِبْرَاهِيمُ بْنُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بن أبي شيبة الكوفي، حدثنا مِنْجَاب بْنُ الْحَارِثِ التَّمِيمِيُّ حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو عَامِرٍ الأسَدِيَ، حَدَّثَنَا سُفْيَانُ، عَنْ عُبَيْدٍ المُكْتب، عَنْ فُضَيل بْنِ عَمْرٍو الفُقَيمي، عَنِ الشَّعْبِيِّ، عَنْ أَنَسِ بْنِ مَالِكٍ قَالَ: كُنَّا عِنْدَ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ فَضْحِكَ حَتَّى بَدَتْ نَوَاجذُه، ثُمَّ قَالَ: "أَتُدْرُونَ مِمَّ أَضْحَكُ؟ " قُلْنَا: اللَّهُ وَرَسُولُهُ أَعْلَمُ. قَالَ: "مِنْ مُجَادَلَةِ الْعَبْدِ رَبَّهُ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ، يَقُولُ: يَا رَبِّ، أَلَمْ تُجِرْني مِنَ الظُّلْمِ؟ فَيَقُولُ: بَلَى. فَيَقُولُ: لَا أُجِيزُ عليَّ شَاهِدًا إِلَّا مِنْ نَفْسِي. فَيَقُولُ: كَفَى بِنَفْسِكَ الْيَوْمَ عَلَيْكَ شَهِيدًا، وَبِالْكِرَامِ عَلَيْكَ شُهُودًا فَيُخْتَمُ عَلَى فِيهِ، وَيُقَالُ لِأَرْكَانِهِ: انْطِقِي فَتَنْطِقُ بِعَمَلِهِ، ثُمَّ يُخَلِّي بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ الْكَلَامِ، فَيَقُولُ: بُعدًا لَكُنّ وسُحْقًا، فعنكُنَّ كنتُ أُنَاضِلُ".

وَقَدْ رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ وَالنَّسَائِيُّ جَمِيعًا، عَنْ أَبِي بكرِ بنِ أَبِي النَّضْرِ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ عُبَيد اللَّهِ الْأَشْجَعِيِّ، عَنْ سُفْيَانَ الثَّوْرِيِّ، بِهِ ثُمَّ قَالَ النَّسَائِيُّ: لَا أَعْلَمُ أَحَدًا رَوَى هَذَا الْحَدِيثَ عَنْ سُفْيَانَ الثَّوْرِيِّ غَيْرَ الْأَشْجَعِيِّ، وَهُوَ حَدِيثٌ غَرِيبٌ، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ. هَكَذَا قَالَ.

وَقَالَ قَتَادَةُ: ابْنَ آدَمَ، وَاللَّهِ إِنَّ عَلَيْكَ لَشُهودًا غيرَ مُتَّهَمَةٍ مِنْ بَدَنِكَ، فَرَاقِبْهُمْ وَاتَّقِ اللَّهَ فِي سِرِّكَ وَعَلَانِيَتِكَ، فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَخْفَى عَلَيْهِ خَافِيَةٌ، وَالظُّلْمَةُ عِنْدَهُ ضَوْءٌ وَالسِّرُّ عِنْدَهُ عَلَانِيَةٌ، فَمَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ أَنْ يَمُوتَ وَهُوَ بِاللَّهِ حَسَنُ الظَّنِّ، فَلْيَفْعَلْ وَلَا قُوَّةَ إِلَّا بِاللَّهِ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿يَوْمَئِذٍ يُوَفِّيهِمُ اللَّهُ دِينَهُمُ الْحَقَّ﴾ قَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿دِينَهُمُ﴾ أَيْ: حِسَابَهُمْ، وَكُلُّ مَا فِي الْقُرْآنِ ﴿دِينَهُمُ﴾ أَيْ: حِسَابَهُمْ. وَكَذَا قَالَ غَيْرُ وَاحِدٍ.

ثُمَّ إِنَّ قِرَاءَةَ الْجُمْهُورِ بِنَصْبِ ﴿الْحَقَّ﴾ عَلَى أَنَّهُ صِفَةٌ لِدِينِهِمْ، وَقَرَأَ مُجَاهِدٌ بِالرَّفْعِ، عَلَى أَنَّهُ نَعَتُ الْجَلَالَةِ. وَقَرَأَهَا بَعْضُ السَّلَفِ فِي مُصْحَفِ أُبَيِّ بْنِ كَعْبٍ: "يَوْمَئِذٍ يُوَفِّيهِمُ اللَّهُ الْحَقُّ دِينَهُمْ" .

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَيَعْلَمُونَ أَنَّ اللَّهَ هُوَ الْحَقُّ الْمُبِينُ﴾ أَيْ: وَعْدُهُ وَوَعِيدُهُ وَحِسَابُهُ هُوَ الْعَدْلُ، الَّذِي لَا جَوْرَ فِيهِ.

---

## 24:26 — verse 26

### Translation

Ibn Abbas said: "The evil sayings are for the evil among men, and the evil among men are for the evil sayings. And the good sayings are for the good among men, and the good among men are for the good sayings." He said: "And it was revealed concerning Aishah and the people of the slander (ahl al-ifk)."

This was likewise narrated from Mujahid, Ata, Sa'id ibn Jubayr, al-Sha'bi, al-Hasan ibn Abi al-Hasan al-Basri, Habib ibn Abi Thabit, and al-Dahhak. Ibn Jarir chose this view, and explained it on the grounds that vile speech is more fitting for the vile among people, and good speech is more fitting for the good among people. So whatever the people of hypocrisy attributed to Aishah, they themselves are more deserving of it, while she is more deserving of innocence and purity from it than they are. This is why He said: {Those are declared innocent of what they say}.

Abd al-Rahman ibn Zayd ibn Aslam said: "The evil among women are for the evil among men, and the evil among men are for the evil among women. And the good among women are for the good among men, and the good among men are for the good among women."

This too, by necessary implication, comes back to what the former said, meaning: Allah would not have made Aishah a wife for the Messenger of Allah ﷺ unless she were good, for he ﷺ is more excellent than every excellent one among mankind, and had she been evil she would not have been fit for him, neither by the Sacred Law nor by divine decree. This is why He said: {Those are declared innocent of what they say}, meaning: they are far removed from what the people of slander and transgression say. {For them is forgiveness}, meaning: on account of the lies said about them, {and a generous provision}, meaning: with Allah in the Gardens of Bliss. In this is a promise that the wife of the Prophet ﷺ would be in Paradise.

Ibn Abi Hatim said: [chain] Yahya ibn al-Jazzar said: Usayr ibn Jabir came to Abdullah and said: "I heard al-Walid ibn Uqbah say something that pleased me." Abdullah said: "The believing man may have in his heart a word that is not good, which churns within his breast and does not settle until he utters it, and a man near him hears it, seizes upon it, and draws it to himself. And the sinful man may have in his heart a good word, which churns within his breast and does not settle until he utters it, and the man near him hears it, seizes upon it, and draws it to himself." Then Abdullah recited: {The evil sayings are for the evil, and the evil are for the evil sayings, and the good sayings are for the good, and the good are for the good sayings}.

Similar to this is what Imam Ahmad related in the Musnad as a marfu (elevated) report: "The likeness of one who hears wisdom and then relates nothing but the worst of what he heard is like a man who came to the owner of a flock of sheep and said: 'Slaughter a sheep for me.' He said: 'Go and take hold of the ear of whichever one you wish.' So he went and took hold of the ear of the sheepdog." And in another hadith: "Wisdom is the lost property of the believer; wherever he finds it, he takes it."

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

قَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ: الْخَبِيثَاتُ مِنَ الْقَوْلِ لِلْخَبِيثِينِ مِنَ الرِّجَالِ، وَالْخَبِيثُونَ مِنَ الرِّجَالِ لِلْخَبِيثَاتِ مِنَ الْقَوْلِ. وَالطَّيِّبَاتُ مِنَ الْقَوْلِ، لِلطَّيِّبِينَ مِنَ الرِّجَالِ، وَالطَّيِّبُونَ مِنَ الرِّجَالِ لِلطَّيِّبَاتِ مِنَ الْقَوْلِ. قَالَ: وَنَزَلَتْ فِي عَائِشَةَ وَأَهْلِ الْإِفْكِ.

وَهَكَذَا رُوي عَنْ مُجَاهِدٍ، وَعَطَاءٍ، وَسَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَير، وَالشَّعْبِيِّ، وَالْحَسَنِ بْنِ أَبِي الْحَسَنِ الْبَصَرِيِّ، وَحَبِيبِ بْنِ أَبِي ثَابِتٍ، وَالضَّحَّاكِ. وَاخْتَارَهُ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ، ووجَّهَهُ بِأَنَّ الْكَلَامَ الْقَبِيحَ أَوْلَى بِأَهْلِ الْقُبْحِ مِنَ النَّاسِ، وَالْكَلَامَ الطَّيِّبَ أَوْلَى بِالطَّيِّبِينَ مِنَ النَّاسِ، فَمَا نَسَبَهُ أَهْلُ النِّفَاقِ إِلَى عائشة هم أَوْلَى بِهِ، وَهِيَ أَوْلَى بِالْبَرَاءَةِ وَالنَّزَاهَةِ مِنْهُمْ؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ: ﴿أُولَئِكَ مُبَرَّءُونَ مِمَّا يَقُولُونَ﴾ .

وَقَالَ عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ زَيْدِ بْنِ أَسْلَمَ: الْخَبِيثَاتُ مِنَ النِّسَاءِ لِلْخَبِيثِينِ مِنَ الرِّجَالِ، وَالْخِبِيثُونَ مِنَ الرِّجَالِ لِلْخَبِيثَاتِ مِنَ النِّسَاءِ، وَالطَّيِّبَاتُ مِنَ النِّسَاءِ لِلطَّيِّبِينَ مِنَ الرِّجَالِ، وَالطَّيِّبُونَ مِنَ الرِّجَالِ لِلطَّيِّبَاتِ مِنَ النِّسَاءِ.

وَهَذَا -أَيْضًا -يَرْجِعُ إِلَى مَا قَالَهُ أُولَئِكَ بِاللَّازِمِ، أَيْ: مَا كَانَ اللَّهُ لِيَجْعَلَ عَائِشَةَ زَوْجَةً لِرَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ إِلَّا وَهِيَ طَيِّبَةٌ؛ لِأَنَّهُ أَطْيَبُ مِنْ كُلِّ طَيِّبٍ مِنَ الْبَشَرِ، وَلَوْ كَانَتْ خَبِيثَةً لَمَا صَلَحَتْ لَهُ، لَا شَرْعًا وَلَا قَدَرًا؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ: ﴿أُولَئِكَ مُبَرَّءُونَ مِمَّا يَقُولُونَ﴾ أَيْ: هُمْ بُعَداء عَمَّا يَقُولُهُ أَهْلُ الْإِفْكِ وَالْعُدْوَانِ، ﴿لَهُمْ مَغْفِرَةٌ﴾ أَيْ: بِسَبَبِ مَا قِيلَ فِيهِمْ مِنَ الْكَذِبِ، ﴿وَرِزْقٌ كَرِيمٌ﴾ أَيْ: عِنْدَ اللَّهِ فِي جَنَّاتِ النَّعِيمِ. وَفِيهِ وَعْدٌ بِأَنْ تَكُونَ زَوْجَةُ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ فِي الْجَنَّةِ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ: حَدَّثَنَا مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ مُسْلِمٍ، حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو نُعَيْمٍ، حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ السَّلَامِ بْنُ حَرْبٍ، عَنْ يَزِيدَ بْنِ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ، عَنْ الْحَكَمِ، عَنْ يَحْيَى بْنِ الْجَزَّارِ قَالَ: جَاءَ أُسَيْرُ بْنُ جَابِرٍ إِلَى عَبْدِ اللَّهِ فَقَالَ: لَقَدْ سَمِعْتُ الْوَلِيدَ بْنَ عُقْبَةَ تَكَلَّمَ بِكَلَامٍ أَعْجَبَنِي. فَقَالَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ: إِنَّ الرَّجُلَ الْمُؤْمِنَ يَكُونُ فِي قَلْبِهِ الْكَلِمَةُ غَيْرَ طَيِّبَةٍ تَتَجَلْجَلُ فِي صَدْرِهِ مَا تَسْتَقِرُّ حَتَّى يَلْفِظَهَا، فَيَسْمَعَهَا رَجُلٌ عِنْدَهُ يَتُلّها فَيَضُمُّهَا إِلَيْهِ. وَإِنَّ الرَّجُلَ الْفَاجِرَ يَكُونُ فِي قَلْبِهِ الْكَلِمَةُ الطَّيِّبَةُ تَتَجَلْجَلُ فِي صَدْرِهِ مَا تَسْتَقِرُّ حَتَّى يَلْفِظَهَا، فَيَسْمَعَهَا الرَّجُلُ الَّذِي عِنْدَهُ يَتُلُّها فَيَضُمُّهَا إِلَيْهِ، ثُمَّ قَرَأَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ: ﴿الْخَبِيثَاتُ لِلْخَبِيثِينَ وَالْخَبِيثُونَ لِلْخَبِيثَاتِ وَالطَّيِّبَاتُ لِلطَّيِّبِينَ وَالطَّيِّبُونَ لِلطَّيِّبَاتِ﴾ .

وَيُشْبِهُ هَذَا مَا رَوَاهُ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ فِي الْمُسْنَدِ مَرْفُوعًا: "مِثْلَ الَّذِي يَسْمَعُ الْحِكْمَةَ ثُمَّ لَا يُحدِّث إِلَّا بشرِّ مَا سَمِعَ، كَمَثَلِ رَجُلٍ جَاءَ إِلَى صَاحِبِ غَنَمٍ، فَقَالَ: أجْزِرني شَاةً. فَقَالَ: اذْهَبْ فَخُذ بأذُن أَيِّهَا شئتَ. فَذَهَبَ فَأَخَذَ بِأُذُنِ كَلْب الْغَنَمِ" وَفِي الْحَدِيثِ الْآخَرِ: "الْحِكْمَةُ ضَالَّةُ الْمُؤْمِنِ حَيْثُ وَجَدَهَا أَخَذَهَا" .

---

## 24:27-29 — verses 27-29 (shared commentary)

### Translation

These are legal manners with which God instructed His believing servants. Regarding seeking permission, God commanded the believers not to enter houses other than their own until they have "sought familiarity" (istaanasu), that is, they should ask permission before entering and give the greeting of peace after entering. One should ask permission three times; if permission is granted, well and good, otherwise one should withdraw, as is established in the authentic collection: that Abu Musa, when he sought permission to enter upon Umar three times and was not granted permission, withdrew. Then Umar said: "Did I not hear the voice of Abdullah ibn Qays asking for permission? Let him in." They sought him and found that he had gone. When he came afterward, Umar said: "What made you turn back?" He said: "I sought permission three times and was not granted it, and I heard the Messenger of God ﷺ say: 'If one of you seeks permission three times and is not granted it, let him withdraw.'" Umar said: "You must bring proof of this, or I will beat you painfully." So he went to a gathering of the Ansar and told them what Umar had said. They said: "None but our youngest will testify for you." So Abu Sa'id al-Khudri stood up with him and informed Umar of this. Umar said: "I was distracted from it by trading in the markets."

Imam Ahmad said: [chain] from Anas, or someone else, that the Messenger of God ﷺ sought permission to enter upon Sa'd ibn Ubadah and said: "Peace be upon you and the mercy of God." Sa'd said: "And upon you be peace and the mercy of God," but he did not let the Prophet ﷺ hear it, until the Prophet had given the greeting three times, and Sa'd had returned it three times without letting him hear it. The Prophet ﷺ then turned back, and Sa'd followed him and said: "O Messenger of God, by my father and mother, every greeting you gave reached my ear, and I did return it to you but did not let you hear it, for I wished to have more of your greeting and of the blessing." Then he brought him into the house and set before him raisins, and the Prophet of God ate. When he had finished, he said: "The righteous have eaten your food, the angels have prayed for you, and those who were fasting have broken their fast with you."

Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i related, from the hadith of Abu Amr al-Awza'i: I heard Yahya ibn Abi Kathir say: Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Sa'd ibn Zurarah related to me, from Qays ibn Sa'd, that is, the son of Ubadah, who said: The Messenger of God ﷺ visited us at our house and said: "Peace be upon you and the mercy of God." Sa'd returned the greeting quietly. Qays said: I said, "Will you not let the Messenger of God ﷺ in?" He said: "Leave him, so that he may give us more of the greeting." The Messenger of God ﷺ said again: "Peace be upon you and the mercy of God." Sa'd again returned it quietly. Then the Messenger of God ﷺ said: "Peace be upon you and the mercy of God." Then the Messenger of God ﷺ turned back, and Sa'd followed him and said: "O Messenger of God, I was hearing your greeting and returning it to you quietly, so that you would give us more of the greeting." He said: So the Messenger of God ﷺ went back with him, and Sa'd ordered water for him to wash, and he washed, then he gave him a wrap dyed with saffron, or wars, and he wrapped himself in it. Then the Messenger of God ﷺ raised his hands, saying: "O God, place Your blessing and mercy upon the family of Sa'd ibn Ubadah." He said: Then the Messenger of God ﷺ ate some of the food, and when he wished to leave, Sa'd brought forward a donkey on which he had placed a saddlecloth, and the Messenger of God ﷺ rode it. Sa'd said: "O Qays, accompany the Messenger of God ﷺ." Qays said: The Messenger of God ﷺ said, "Ride," but I refused. He said, "Either ride or go back." Qays said: So I went back.

This has been related through another route as well, and it is a good, strong hadith. God knows best.

It should be known that one who seeks permission to enter upon the people of a house should not stand directly facing the door, but rather let the door be to his right or his left. This is based on what Abu Dawud related: [chain] from Abdullah ibn Busr, who said: When the Messenger of God ﷺ came to the door of a people, he would not face the door directly, but would stand to its right corner or its left corner, and he would say: "Peace be upon you, peace be upon you." This was because in those days houses had no curtains over their doors. Abu Dawud alone related this.

Abu Dawud also said: [chain], from Huzayl, who said: A man came, Uthman said it was Sa'd, and stood at the door of the Prophet ﷺ seeking permission, and he stood at the door, Uthman said, facing the door directly. The Prophet ﷺ said to him: "Like this, away from it, or thus," for seeking permission is on account of looking.

Abu Dawud al-Tayalisi related it from Sufyan al-Thawri, from al-A'mash, from Talha ibn Musarrif, from a man, from Sa'd, from the Prophet ﷺ. Abu Dawud related it from his hadith.

In the two authentic collections, from the Messenger of God ﷺ, that he said: "If a man were to look into your house without permission and you threw a pebble at him and put out his eye, there would be no blame upon you."

The group [of hadith compilers] related, from the hadith of Shu'bah, from Muhammad ibn al-Munkadir, from Jabir, who said: I came to the Prophet ﷺ regarding a debt that was owed by my father, and I knocked on the door. He said: "Who is that?" I said: "It is I." He said: "I, I," as though he disliked it.

He disliked this because this expression does not identify the speaker until he makes clear his name or the byname by which he is known. Otherwise, everyone expresses himself by saying "I," and thus the purpose of seeking permission, which is the "seeking of familiarity" commanded in the verse, is not achieved.

Al-Awfi said, from Ibn Abbas: "Seeking familiarity" means seeking permission. Others besides him said the same.

Ibn Jarir said: [chain], from Ibn Abbas, regarding this verse, {Do not enter houses other than your own houses until you have sought familiarity and greeted with peace}: he said, it is simply an error of the scribe, it should be "until you have sought permission and greeted with peace."

Hushaym related it likewise from Abu Bishr, who is Ja'far ibn Iyas, with the same wording. Mu'adh ibn Sulayman related from Ja'far ibn Iyas, from Sa'id, from Ibn Abbas, the same, and added: Ibn Abbas used to recite it as "until you have sought permission and greeted with peace," and he used to recite according to the reading of Ubayy ibn Ka'b, may God be pleased with him.

This is a very unusual (gharib) report from Ibn Abbas.

Hushaym said: [chain], from Ibrahim, who said: In the copy of the Qur'an of Ibn Mas'ud it reads: "until you have greeted its people with peace and sought permission." This too is a report from Ibn Abbas, and it is the preference of Ibn Jarir.

Imam Ahmad said: [chain], that Kaladah ibn al-Hanbal informed him, that Safwan ibn Umayyah sent him during the conquest with fresh milk, a young goat, and cucumbers, while the Prophet ﷺ was at the upper part of the valley. He said: I entered upon him without greeting and without seeking permission. The Prophet ﷺ said: "Go back and say: Peace be upon you, may I enter?" This was after Safwan had accepted Islam.

Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and al-Nasa'i related it from the hadith of Ibn Jurayj, with the same wording, and al-Tirmidhi said: it is hasan gharib (a good but singular report), we do not know it except from his hadith.

Abu Dawud said: [chain], from Rib'i, who said: A man from Banu Amir told us that he sought permission to enter upon the Prophet ﷺ while he was in his house, and he said, "May I enter?" The Prophet ﷺ said to his servant: "Go out to this man and teach him how to seek permission; tell him to say: Peace be upon you, may I enter?" The man heard this and said: "Peace be upon you, may I enter?" So the Prophet ﷺ gave him permission, and he entered.

Hushaym said: [chain], from Amr ibn Sa'id al-Thaqafi, that a man sought permission to enter upon the Prophet ﷺ and said, "May I enter?" or "shall we enter?" The Prophet ﷺ said to a slave girl of his called Rawdah: "Go to this man and teach him, for he does not know how to seek permission properly; tell him to say: Peace be upon you, may I enter?" The man heard this and said it, and the Prophet said: "Enter."

Al-Tirmidhi said: [chain], from Jabir ibn Abdullah, who said: The Messenger of God ﷺ said: "The greeting of peace comes before speech."

Then al-Tirmidhi said: Anbasah is weak in hadith and unreliable, and Muhammad ibn Zadhan is one whose hadith is considered objectionable (munkar).

Hushaym said: Mughira said: Mujahid said: Ibn Umar came back from an errand, and the scorching ground had hurt him, so he came to the tent of a woman from Quraysh and said: "Peace be upon you, may I enter?" She said: "Enter with peace." He repeated it, and she repeated her answer, while he was shifting his weight between his feet. He said: "Say: enter." She said: "Enter," so he entered.

Ibn Abi Hatim said: Abu Sa'id al-Ashajj told us, Abu Nu'aym al-Ahwal told us, Khalid ibn Iyas told us, my grandmother Umm Iyas told me, she said: I was among four women seeking permission to enter [upon Aisha], and I said: "May we enter?" She said: "No, tell your companion to seek permission properly." So she said: "Peace be upon you, may we enter?" She said: "Enter," then she said: {O you who believe, do not enter houses other than your own houses until you have sought familiarity (ta'anus, sought to make your presence known) and greeted their people with peace} [the verse].

Hushaym said: Ash'ath ibn Sawwar informed us, from Kurdus, from Ibn Mas'ud, who said: "You must seek permission to enter upon your mothers and your sisters." Ash'ath said, from Adi ibn Thabit: A woman from the Ansar said: "O Messenger of Allah, I am sometimes in my house in a state in which I would not like anyone to see me, neither father nor son, yet a man from my household keeps entering upon me while I am in that state." He said: So there was revealed: {O you who believe, do not enter houses other than your own houses until you have sought familiarity and greeted their people with peace}.

Ibn Jurayj said: I heard Ata ibn Abi Rabah reporting from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: "There are three verses which people have denied. Allah said: {Indeed the most noble of you in the sight of Allah is the most God-fearing of you} [al-Hujurat: 13], yet people say: the most noble of them in the sight of Allah is the one with the greatest house. And the whole matter of seeking permission to enter, people have denied it entirely." He said: I said: "Must I seek permission to enter upon my sisters, orphans under my guardianship, who are with me in one house?" He said: "Yes." I pressed him again hoping he would grant me a concession, but he refused. He said: "Would you like to see her naked?" I said: "No." He said: "Then seek permission." He said: I pressed him again, and he said: "Would you like to obey Allah?" I said: "Yes." He said: "Then seek permission."

Ibn Jurayj said: Ibn Tawus informed me, from his father, who said: "There is no woman whose nakedness I would more dislike to see than one who is a mahram (a relative within the forbidden degrees of marriage)." He said: he used to be strict about that.

Ibn Jurayj said, from al-Zuhri: I heard Huzayl ibn Shurahbil al-Awdi, the blind, that he heard Ibn Mas'ud say: "You must seek permission to enter upon your mothers."

Ibn Jurayj said: I said to Ata: "Does a man seek permission to enter upon his own wife?" He said: "No."

This is to be understood as meaning it is not obligatory; otherwise, it is more fitting that he inform her of his entrance and not surprise her with it, in case she might be in a state in which she would not like him to see her.

Abu Ja'far ibn Jarir said: al-Qasim told us, [he said] al-Husayn told us, Muhammad ibn Hazim told us, from al-A'mash, from Amr ibn Murrah, from Yahya ibn al-Jazzar, from the nephew of Zaynab, the wife of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, from Zaynab, may Allah be pleased with her, who said: "When Abdullah came back from an errand and reached the door, he would clear his throat and spit, disliking to burst in upon us in some matter he would dislike." This is a sound chain.

Ibn Abi Hatim said: Ahmad ibn Sinan al-Wasiti told us, Abdullah ibn Numayr told us, al-A'mash told us, from Amr ibn Murrah, from Abu Hubayrah, who said: "When Abdullah entered the house he would seek familiarity (ista'nas), that is, he would speak and raise his voice."

Mujahid said regarding {until you have sought familiarity}: "It means to clear one's throat, or to spit lightly."

It is reported from Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal, may Allah have mercy on him, that he said: "When a man enters his house, it is recommended for him to clear his throat, or to make the sound of his sandals."

For this reason, it has come in the Sahih from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ that he forbade a man from suddenly showing up upon his family unannounced at night, and in another narration: "at night, catching them off guard."

In another hadith: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ arrived at Madinah during the day, and had his camel kneel outside it, and said: "Wait until it is evening," meaning the latter part of the day, "so that the disheveled woman may comb her hair, and the one whose husband has been away may shave herself."

Ibn Abi Hatim said: my father told us, Abu Bakr ibn Abi Shaybah told us, Abdul-Rahman ibn Sulayman told us, from Wasil ibn al-Sa'ib, Abu Sawrah, nephew of Abu Ayyub, told me, from Abu Ayyub, who said: I said: "O Messenger of Allah, this is the greeting of peace, but what is al-isti'nas (seeking familiarity)?" He said: "A man speaks a phrase of glorification, of magnification, and of praise, and clears his throat, thereby alerting the household." This is a gharib (singular) hadith.

Qatada said regarding His saying {until you have sought familiarity}: "It means seeking permission to enter." He said: it used to be said: seeking permission to enter is three times, and whoever is not granted permission after them should return. As for the first time: so that the household may hear. As for the second: so that they may take their precautions. As for the third: if they wish they grant permission, and if they wish they decline. Do not stand at the door of people who have turned you away from their door, for people have their needs and their occupations, and Allah is more deserving that an excuse be accepted.

Muqatil ibn Hayyan said regarding His saying {O you who believe, do not enter houses other than your own houses until you have sought familiarity and greeted their people with peace}: In the Jahiliyyah (pre-Islamic era), when a man met his companion, he would not greet him with peace, but would say: "May you be given life in the morning, and may you be given life in the evening," and that was the greeting of the people among themselves. And one of them would go to his companion and would not seek permission, but would simply burst in and say: "I have entered." This caused hardship for the man, for perhaps he would be with his family. So Allah changed all of that, into modesty and chastity, and made it pure and free from filth, dirt, and impurity, so He said: {O you who believe, do not enter houses other than your own houses until you have sought familiarity and greeted their people with peace}.

What Muqatil said here is good; and for this reason He said: {That is better for you}, meaning: seeking permission is better for you, in the sense that it is better for both parties, for the one seeking permission and for the household, {that you may remember}.

His saying: {But if you find no one therein, do not enter it until permission is given to you}, and that is because of what it would involve, of disposing of another's property without his permission. If he wishes, he grants permission, and if he wishes, he does not. {And if it is said to you, "Go back," then go back, it is purer for you}, that is: if they turn you away from the door, whether before permission or after it, {then go back, it is purer for you}, meaning: your going back is purer for you and cleaner, {And Allah knows well what you do}.

Qatada said: Some of the Muhajirun said: "I sought this verse my whole life but never fully attained it, that I should seek permission to enter upon some of my brothers, and he would say to me: 'Go back,' and I would go back rejoicing," because of His saying, {And if it is said to you, "Go back," then go back, it is purer for you, and Allah knows well what you do}.

Sa'id ibn Jubayr said: {And if it is said to you, "Go back," then go back}, meaning: do not linger at people's doors.

His saying: {There is no blame upon you that you enter houses not inhabited, in which you have some interest, and Allah knows what you reveal and what you conceal}. This noble verse is more specific than the one before it, in that it entails the permissibility of entering houses in which there is no one, if he has some interest in them, without seeking permission, like a house prepared for a guest, if he has been given permission for it the first time, that suffices.

Ibn Jurayj said: Ibn Abbas said: {Do not enter houses other than your own houses}, then this was abrogated and an exception was made, for He said: {There is no blame upon you that you enter houses not inhabited, in which you have some interest}. The same has been reported from Ikrima and al-Hasan al-Basri.

Others said: these are the houses of merchants, such as inns and travelers' lodgings, and the houses of Makkah, and the like. Ibn Jarir preferred this view, and related it from a group of scholars. But the first view is more apparent, and Allah knows best.

Malik said, from Zayd ibn Aslam: "They are tent-houses (houses of hair, i.e., tents)."

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

هَذِهِ آدَابٌ شَرْعِيَّةٌ، أَدَّبَ اللَّهُ بِهَا عِبَادَهُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ، وَذَلِكَ فِي الِاسْتِئْذَانِ أَمَرَ اللَّهُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ أَلَّا يَدْخُلُوا بُيُوتًا غَيْرَ بُيُوتِهِمْ حَتَّى يَسْتَأْنِسُوا، أَيْ: يَسْتَأْذِنُوا قَبْلَ الدُّخُولِ وَيُسَلِّمُوا بَعْدَهُ. وَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَسْتَأْذِنَ ثَلَاثًا، فَإِنْ أُذِنَ لَهُ، وَإِلَّا انْصَرَفَ، كَمَا ثَبَتَ فِي الصَّحِيحِ: أَنَّ أَبَا مُوسَى حِينَ اسْتَأْذَنَ عَلَى عُمَرَ ثَلَاثًا، فَلَمْ يُؤْذَنْ لَهُ، انْصَرَفَ. ثُمَّ قَالَ عُمَرُ: أَلَمْ أَسْمَعْ صَوْتَ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ قَيْسٍ يَسْتَأْذِنُ؟ ائْذَنُوا لَهُ. فَطَلَبُوهُ فَوَجَدُوهُ قَدْ ذَهَبَ، فَلَمَّا جَاءَ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ قَالَ: مَا رَجَعَك؟ قَالَ: إِنِّي اسْتَأْذَنْتُ ثَلَاثًا فَلَمْ يُؤْذَنْ لِي، وَإِنِّي سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وسلم يَقُولُ: "إِذَا اسْتَأْذَنَ أَحَدُكُمْ ثَلَاثًا، فَلَمْ يُؤْذَنْ لَهُ، فَلْيَنْصَرِفْ". فَقَالَ: لَتَأتِيَنَّ عَلَى هَذَا بِبَيِّنَةٍ وَإِلَّا أَوْجَعْتُكَ ضَرْبًا. فَذَهَبَ إِلَى مَلَأٍ مِنَ الْأَنْصَارِ، فَذَكَرَ لَهُمْ مَا قَالَ عُمَرُ، فَقَالُوا: لَا يَشْهَدُ لَكَ إِلَّا أَصْغَرُنَا. فَقَامَ مَعَهُ أَبُو سَعِيدٍ الخُدْريّ فَأَخْبَرَ عُمَرَ بِذَلِكَ، فَقَالَ: أَلْهَانِي عَنْهُ الصَّفْق بِالْأَسْوَاقِ .

وَقَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثنا عَبْدُ الرَّزَّاقِ، أَخْبَرَنَا مَعْمَر عَنْ ثَابِتٍ، عَنْ أَنَسٍ -أَوْ: غَيْرِهِ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ اسْتَأْذَنَ عَلَى سَعْدِ بْنِ عُبَادَةَ فَقَالَ:"السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكَ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ". فَقَالَ سَعْدٌ: وَعَلَيْكَ السَّلَامُ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ وَلَمْ يَسْمَعِ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ حَتَّى سَلَّمَ ثَلَاثًا. وَرَدَّ عَلَيْهِ سَعْدٌ ثَلَاثًا وَلَمْ يُسْمعه. فَرَجَعَ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ، وَاتَّبَعَهُ سَعْدٌ فَقَالَ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، بِأَبِي أَنْتَ وَأُمِّي، مَا سلمتَ تَسْلِيمَةً إِلَّا وَهِيَ بِأُذُنِي، وَلَقَدْ رَدَدْت عَلَيْكَ وَلَمْ أُسْمِعك، وأردتُ أَنْ أَسْتَكْثِرَ مِنْ سَلَامِكِ وَمِنَ الْبَرَكَةِ. ثُمَّ أَدْخَلَهُ الْبَيْتَ، فقرَّب إِلَيْهِ زَبيبًا، فَأَكَلَ نَبِيُّ اللَّهِ. فَلَمَّا فَرَغَ قَالَ: "أَكَلَ طَعَامَكُمُ الْأَبْرَارُ، وصَلَّت عَلَيْكُمُ الْمَلَائِكَةُ، وَأَفْطَرَ عِنْدَكُمُ الصَّائِمُونَ" .

وَقَدْ رَوَى أَبُو دَاوُدَ وَالنَّسَائِيُّ، مِنْ حَدِيثِ أَبِي عَمْرٍو الْأَوْزَاعِيِّ: سَمِعْتُ يَحْيَى بْنَ أَبِي كَثِيرٍ يَقُولُ: حَدَّثَنِي مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ سَعْدِ بْنِ زُرَارَةَ، عَنْ قَيْسِ بْنِ سَعْدٍ -هُوَ ابْنُ عِبَادَةَ -قَالَ: زَارَنَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ فِي مَنْزِلِنَا، فَقَالَ: "السلام عليكم ورحمة الله". فرد سعد ردا خَفِيًّا ، قَالَ قَيْسٌ: فَقُلْتُ: أَلَا تَأْذَنُ لِرَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ؟ فَقَالَ: ذَرْه يُكْثِرْ عَلَيْنَا مِنَ السَّلَامُ. فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ:"السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ". فَرَدَّ سَعْدٌ رَدًا خَفِيًّا ، ثُمَّ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: " السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ" ثُمَّ رَجَع رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ، وَاتَّبَعَهُ سَعْدٌ فَقَالَ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، إِنِّي كُنْتُ أَسْمَعُ تَسْلِيمَكَ، وَأَرُدُّ عَلَيْكَ رَدًّا خَفِيًّا ، لِتُكْثِرَ عَلَيْنَا مِنَ السَّلَامِ. قَالَ: فَانْصَرَفَ مَعَهُ [رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ، فَأَمَرَ لَهُ سَعْدٌ بِغُسْلٍ، فَاغْتَسَلَ، ثُمَّ نَاوَلَهُ ملْحَفَة مَصْبُوغَةً] بِزَعْفَرَانٍ -أَوْ: وَرس -فَاشْتَمَلَ بِهَا، ثُمَّ رَفَعَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ يَدَيْهِ وَهُوَ يَقُولُ: "اللَّهُمَّ اجْعَلْ صَلَاتَكَ وَرَحْمَتَكَ عَلَى آلِ سَعْدِ بْنِ عُبَادَةَ". قَالَ: ثُمَّ أَصَابَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ مِنَ الطَّعَامِ، فَلَمَّا أَرَادَ الِانْصِرَافَ قَرَّبَ إِلَيْهِ سَعْدٌ حِمَارًا قَدْ وَطَّأ عَلَيْهِ بِقَطِيفَةٍ، فَرَكِبَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ فَقَالَ سَعْدٌ: يَا قَيْسُ، اصحب رسول اللَّهِ ﷺ. قَالَ قَيْسٌ: فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "ارْكَبْ". فَأَبَيْتُ، فَقَالَ: "إِمَّا أَنْ تَرْكَبَ وَإِمَّا أَنْ تَنْصَرِفَ". قَالَ: فَانْصَرَفْتُ.

وَقَدْ رُوِيَ هَذَا مِنْ وَجْهٍ آخَرَ فَهُوَ حَدِيثٌ جَيِّدٌ قَوِيٌّ، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

ثُمَّ ليُعْلمْ أَنَّهُ يَنْبَغِي لِلْمُسْتَأْذِنِ عَلَى أَهْلِ الْمَنْزِلِ أَلَّا يَقِفَ تِلْقَاءَ الْبَابِ بِوَجْهِهِ، وَلَكِنْ ليَكن البابُ، عَنْ يَمِينِهِ أَوْ يَسَارِهِ؛ لِمَا رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ: حَدَّثَنَا مُؤَمَّل بْنُ الْفَضْلِ الْحَرَّانَيُّ -فِي آخَرِينَ -قَالُوا: حَدَّثَنَا بَقيَّة، حَدَّثَنَا مُحَمَّدُ بْنِ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ بُسْر قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ إِذَا أَتَى بَابَ قَوْمٍ، لَمْ يَسْتَقْبِلِ الْبَابَ مِنْ تِلْقَاءِ وَجْهِهِ، وَلَكِنْ مِنْ رُكْنِهِ الْأَيْمَنِ أَوِ الْأَيْسَرِ، وَيَقُولُ: "السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ، السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ". وَذَلِكَ أَنَّ الدُّورَ لَمْ يَكُنْ عَلَيْهَا يَوْمئِذٍ سُتُورٌ. تَفَرد بِهِ أَبُو دَاوُدَ .

وَقَالَ أَبُو دَاوُدَ أَيْضًا: حَدَّثَنَا عُثْمَانُ بْنُ أَبِي شَيْبَةَ، حَدَّثَنَا جَرِيرٌ، (ح) قَالَ أَبُو دَاوُدَ: وَحَدَّثَنَا أَبُو بَكْرِ بْنُ أَبِي شَيْبَةَ، حَدَّثَنَا حَفْصٌ، عَنِ الْأَعْمَشِ، عَنْ طَلْحَةَ، عَنْ هُزَيل قَالَ: جَاءَ رَجُلٌ -قَالَ عُثْمَانُ: سَعْدٌ -فَوَقَفَ عَلَى بَابِ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ يَسْتَأْذِنُ، فَقَامَ عَلَى الْبَابِ -قَالَ عُثْمَانُ: مُسْتَقْبَلَ الْبَابِ -فَقَالَ لَهُ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ: "هَكَذَا عَنْكَ -أَوْ: هَكَذَا -فَإِنَّمَا الِاسْتِئْذَانُ مِنَ النَّظَرِ" .

وَقَدْ رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ الطَّيَالِسِيُّ، عَنْ سُفْيَانَ الثَّوْرِيِّ، عَنِ الْأَعْمَشِ عَنْ طَلْحَةَ بْنِ مُصَرّف، عَنْ رَجُلٍ، عَنْ سَعْدٍ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ. رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ مِنْ حَدِيثِهِ .

وَفِي الصَّحِيحَيْنِ، عَنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ أَنَّهُ قَالَ: "لَوْ أَنَّ امْرَأً اطَّلَعَ عَلَيْكَ بِغَيْرِ إِذَنٍ فَخَذَفته بِحَصَاةٍ، فَفَقَأْتَ عَيْنَهُ، مَا كَانَ عَلَيْكَ مِنْ جُنَاحٍ" .

وَأَخْرَجَ الْجَمَاعَةُ مِنْ حَدِيثِ شُعْبَةَ، عَنْ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ الْمُنْكَدِرِ، عَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: أتيتُ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ فِي دَين كَانَ عَلَى أَبِي، فَدَقَقْتُ الْبَابَ، فَقَالَ: "مَنْ ذَا"؟ قُلْتُ: أَنَا. قَالَ: "أَنَا، أَنَا" كَأَنَّهُ كَرِهَهُ .

وَإِنَّمَا كَرِهَ ذَلِكَ لِأَنَّ هَذِهِ اللَّفْظَةَ لَا يُعرَف صَاحِبُهَا حَتَّى يُفصح بِاسْمِهِ أَوْ كُنْيَتِهِ الَّتِي هُوَ مَشْهُورٌ بِهَا، وَإِلَّا فَكُلُّ أَحَدٍ يُعبِّر عَنْ نَفْسِهِ بِـ"أَنَا"، فَلَا يَحْصُلُ بِهَا الْمَقْصُودُ مِنَ الِاسْتِئْذَانِ، الَّذِي هُوَ الِاسْتِئْنَاسُ الْمَأْمُورُ بِهِ فِي الْآيَةِ.

وَقَالَ العَوْفي، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: الِاسْتِئْنَاسُ: الِاسْتِئْذَانُ. وَكَذَا قَالَ غيرُ وَاحِدٍ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنَا ابْنُ بَشَّار، حَدَّثَنَا مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ جَعْفَرٍ، حَدَّثَنَا شُعْبَةُ، عَنْ أَبِي بِشْر، عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَيْرٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ فِي هَذِهِ الْآيَةِ: ﴿لَا تَدْخُلُوا بُيُوتًا غَيْرَ بُيُوتِكُمْ حَتَّى تَسْتَأْنِسُوا وَتُسَلِّمُوا﴾ قَالَ: إِنَّمَا هِيَ خَطَأٌ مِنَ الْكَاتِبِ، "حَتَّى تَسْتَأذنُوا وَتُسَلِّمُوا".

وَهَكَذَا رَوَاهُ هُشَيم، عَنْ أَبِي بِشْرٍ -وَهُوَ جَعْفَرُ بْنُ إِيَاسٍ -بِهِ. وَرَوَى مُعَاذُ بْنُ سُلَيْمَانَ، عَنْ جَعْفَرِ بْنِ إِيَاسٍ، عَنْ سَعِيدٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، بِمِثْلِهِ، وَزَادَ: وَكَانَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ يَقْرَأُ: "حَتَّى تَسْتَأذنُوا وَتُسَلِّمُوا"، وَكَانَ يَقْرَأُ عَلَى قِرَاءَةِ أُبَيِّ بْنِ كَعْبٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ.

وَهَذَا غَرِيبٌ جِدًّا عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ.

وَقَالَ هُشَيْم أَخْبَرَنَا مُغِيرَةُ، عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: فِي مُصْحَفِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ: "حَتَّى تُسَلِّمُوا عَلَى أَهْلِهَا وَتَسْتَأْذِنُوا". وَهَذَا أَيْضًا رِوَايَةٌ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، وَهُوَ اخْتِيَارُ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ.

وَقَدْ قَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا رَوْح، حَدَّثَنَا ابْنُ جُرَيْج، أَخْبَرَنِي عَمْرُو بْنُ أَبِي سُفْيَانَ: أَنَّ عَمْرَو بْنَ أَبِي صَفْوَانَ أَخْبَرَهُ، أَنَّ كَلَدَةَ بْنَ الْحَنْبَلِ أَخْبَرَهُ، أَنَّ صَفْوَانَ بْنَ أُمَيَّةَ بَعْثَهُ فِي الْفَتْحِ بِلبَأ وجَدَايَة وضَغَابيس، وَالنَّبِيُّ ﷺ بِأَعْلَى الْوَادِي. قَالَ: فدخلتُ عَلَيْهِ وَلَمْ أُسَلِّمْ وَلَمْ أَسْتَأْذِنْ. فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ: "ارْجِعْ فَقُلِ: السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ، أَأَدْخُلُ؟ " وَذَلِكَ بَعْدَمَا أَسْلَمَ صَفْوَانُ.

وَرَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ وَالتِّرْمِذِيُّ وَالنَّسَائِيُّ مِنْ حَدِيثِ ابْنِ جُرَيْجٍ، بِهِ وَقَالَ التِّرْمِذِيُّ: حَسَنٌ غَرِيبٌ، لَا نَعْرِفُهُ إِلَّا مِنْ حَدِيثِهِ.

وَقَالَ أَبُو دَاوُدَ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو بَكْرِ بْنُ أَبِي شَيْبَةَ، حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو الأحوَص، عَنْ مَنْصُورٍ، عَنْ رِبْعي قَالَ: حَدَّثَنَا رَجُلٌ مَنْ بَنِي عَامِرٍ اسْتَأْذَنَ عَلَى النَّبِيَّ ﷺ، وَهُوَ فِي بَيْتِهِ، فَقَالَ: أَأَلِجُ؟ فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ لِخَادِمِهِ: "اخْرُجْ إِلَى هَذَا فعلِّمه الِاسْتِئْذَانَ، فَقُلْ لَهُ: قُلِ: السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ، أَأَدْخُلُ؟ " فَسَمِعَهُ الرَّجُلُ فَقَالَ: السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ، أَأَدْخُلُ؟ فَأَذِنَ لَهُ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ، فَدَخَلَ .

وَقَالَ هُشَيْم: أَخْبَرَنَا مَنْصُورٌ، عَنِ ابْنِ سِيرِين -وَأَخْبَرَنَا يُونُسُ بْنُ عُبَيْدٍ، عَنْ عَمْرو بْنِ سَعِيدٍ الثَّقَفِيِّ -أَنَّ رَجُلًا اسْتَأْذَنَ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ ﷺ فَقَالَ: أَأَلِجُ -أَوْ: أَنَلِجُ؟ -فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ لِأَمَةٍ لَهُ، يُقَالُ لَهَا رَوْضَةُ: "قَوْمِي إِلَى هَذَا فَعَلِّمِيهِ، فَإِنَّهُ لَا يُحْسِنُ يَسْتَأْذِنُ، فَقُولِي لَهُ يَقُولُ: السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ، أَأَدْخُلُ". فَسَمِعَهَا الرَّجُلُ، فَقَالَهَا، فَقَالَ: "ادْخُلْ" .

وَقَالَ التِّرْمِذِيُّ: حَدَّثَنَا الْفَضْلُ بْنُ الصَّبَاحِ، حَدَّثَنَا سَعِيدُ بْنُ زَكَرِيَّا، عَنْ عَنْبَسَة بْنِ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ، عَنْ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ زَاذَانَ، عَنْ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ المنْكَدِر، عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "السَّلَامُ قَبْلَ الْكَلَامِ" .

ثُمَّ قَالَ التِّرْمِذِيُّ: عَنْبَسَةُ ضَعِيفُ الْحَدِيثِ ذَاهِبٌ، وَمُحَمَّدُ بْنُ زَاذَانَ مُنكَر الْحَدِيثِ.

وَقَالَ هُشَيْم: قَالَ مُغِيرَةُ: قَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ: جَاءَ ابْنُ عُمَرَ مِنْ حَاجَةٍ، وَقَدْ آذَاهُ الرَّمْضَاءُ، فأتى فُسْطَاط امْرَأَةٍ مِنْ قُرَيْشٍ، فَقَالَ: السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ، أَأَدْخُلُ؟ قالت: ادخل بسلام. فأعاد، فأعادت، وَهُوَ يُرَاوح بَيْنَ قَدَمَيْهِ، قَالَ: قُولِي: ادْخُلْ. قَالَتِ: ادْخُلْ، فَدَخَلَ .

وَقَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو سَعِيدٍ الْأَشَجُّ، حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو نُعَيْمٍ الْأَحْوَلُ، حَدَّثَنَا خَالِدُ بْنُ إِيَاسٍ، حَدَّثَتْنِي جَدَّتِي أُمُّ إِيَاسٍ قَالَتْ: كُنْتُ فِي أَرْبَعِ نِسْوَةٍ نَسْتَأْذِنُ [عَلَى عَائِشَةَ] فَقُلْتُ: نَدْخُلُ؟ قَالَتْ: لَا قُلْنَ لِصَاحِبَتِكُنَّ: تَسْتَأْذِنُ. فَقَالَتِ: السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ، أَنَدْخُلُ؟ قَالَتِ: ادْخُلُوا، ثُمَّ قَالَتْ: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لَا تَدْخُلُوا بُيُوتًا غَيْرَ بُيُوتِكُمْ حَتَّى تَسْتَأْنِسُوا وَتُسَلِّمُوا عَلَى أَهْلِهَا﴾ [الْآيَةَ] .

وَقَالَ هُشَيْم: أَخْبَرَنَا أَشْعَثُ بْنُ سَوَّار، عَنْ كُرْدُوس، عَنِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: عَلَيْكُمْ أَنْ تَسْتَأْذِنُوا عَلَى أُمَّهَاتِكُمْ وَأَخَوَاتِكُمْ. قَالَ أَشْعَثُ، عَنْ عَدِيِّ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ: إِنَّ امْرَأَةً مِنَ الْأَنْصَارِ قَالَتْ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، إِنِّي أَكُونُ فِي مَنْزِلِي عَلَى الْحَالِ الَّتِي لَا أُحِبُّ أَنْ يَرَانِي أَحَدٌ عَلَيْهَا، وَالِدٌ وَلَا وَلَدٌ، وَإِنَّهُ لَا يَزَالُ يَدْخُلُ عليَّ رَجُلٌ مِنْ أَهْلِي، وَأَنَا عَلَى تِلْكَ الْحَالِ؟ قَالَ: فَنَزَلَتْ: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لَا تَدْخُلُوا بُيُوتًا غَيْرَ بُيُوتِكُمْ حَتَّى تَسْتَأْنِسُوا وَتُسَلِّمُوا عَلَى أَهْلِهَا﴾ .

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جُرَيْجٍ: سَمِعْتُ عَطَاءَ بْنَ أَبِي رَبَاحٍ يُخْبِرُ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، قَالَ: ثَلَاثُ آيَاتٍ جَحَدها النَّاسُ: قَالَ اللَّهُ: ﴿إِنَّ أَكْرَمَكُمْ عِنْدَ اللَّهِ أَتْقَاكُمْ﴾ [الْحُجُرَاتُ: ١٣] ، قَالَ: وَيَقُولُونَ: إِنَّ أَكْرَمَهُمْ عِنْدَ اللَّهِ أَعْظَمُهُمْ بَيْتًا. قَالَ: وَالْإِذْنُ كُلُّهُ قَدْ جَحَدَهُ النَّاسُ. قَالَ: قُلْتُ: أَسْتَأْذِنُ عَلَى أَخَوَاتِي أَيْتَامٍ فِي حِجْرِي، مَعِي فِي بَيْتٍ وَاحِدٍ؟ قَالَ: نَعَمْ. فَرَدَدْتُ ليرخِّص لِي، فَأَبَى. قَالَ: تُحِبُّ أَنْ تَرَاهَا عُرْيَانَةً؟ قُلْتُ: لَا. قَالَ: فَاسْتَأْذِنْ. قَالَ: فَرَاجَعْتُهُ أَيْضًا، فَقَالَ: أَتُحِبُّ أَنْ تُطِيعَ اللَّهَ؟ قُلْتُ: نَعَمْ. قَالَ: فَاسْتَأْذِنْ.

قَالَ ابْنُ جُرَيْج: وَأَخْبَرَنِي ابْنُ طَاوُسٍ عَنْ أَبِيهِ قَالَ: مَا مِنِ امْرَأَةٍ أَكْرَهُ إِلَيَّ أَنْ أَرَى عُرْيَتَهَا مِنْ ذَاتِ مَحْرَمٍ. قَالَ: وَكَانَ يُشَدِّدُ فِي ذَلِكَ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جُرَيْجٍ، عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ: سَمِعْتُ هُزَيل بْنَ شُرَحْبِيل الأوْدِيّ الْأَعْمَى، أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ ابْنَ مَسْعُودٍ يَقُولُ: عَلَيْكُمُ الْإِذْنُ عَلَى أُمَّهَاتِكُمْ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جُرَيْجٍ: قُلْتُ لِعَطَاءٍ: أَيَسْتَأْذِنُ الرَّجُلُ عَلَى امْرَأَتِهِ؟ قَالَ: لَا.

وَهَذَا مَحْمُولٌ عَلَى عَدَمِ الْوُجُوبِ، وَإِلَّا فَالْأَوْلَى أَنْ يُعْلِمَهَا بِدُخُولِهِ وَلَا يُفَاجِئَهَا بِهِ، لِاحْتِمَالِ أَنْ تَكُونَ عَلَى هَيْئَةٍ لَا تُحِبُّ أَنْ يَرَاهَا عَلَيْهَا.

وَقَالَ أَبُو جَعْفَرِ بْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنَا الْقَاسِمُ، [قَالَ] حَدَّثَنَا الْحُسَيْنُ، حَدَّثَنَا مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ حَازِمٍ، عَنِ الْأَعْمَشِ، عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ مُرَّة، عَنْ يَحْيَى بْنِ الْجَزَّارِ، عَنِ ابْنِ أَخِي زَيْنَبَ -امْرَأَةَ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ -، عَنْ زَيْنَبَ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا، قَالَتْ: كَانَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ إِذَا جَاءَ مِنْ حَاجَةٍ فَانْتَهَى إِلَى الْبَابِ، تَنَحْنَحَ وَبَزَقَ؛ كَرَاهِيَةَ أَنْ يهجُم مِنَّا عَلَى أَمْرٍ يَكْرَهُهُ . إِسْنَادٌ صَحِيحٌ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ: حَدَّثَنَا أَحْمَدُ بْنُ سِنَان الْوَاسِطِيُّ، حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ نُمَيْر، حدثنا الأعمش، عن عمرو بن مُرَّة، عن أبي هُبَيْرة قَالَ: كَانَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ إِذَا دَخَلَ الدَّارَ اسْتَأْنَسَ -تَكَلَّمَ وَرَفَعَ صَوْتَهُ.

[وَ] قَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ: ﴿حَتَّى تَسْتَأْنِسُوا﴾ قَالَ: تَنَحْنَحُوا -أَوْ تَنَخَّموا.

وَعَنِ الْإِمَامِ أَحْمَدَ بْنِ حَنْبَلٍ، رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ، أَنَّهُ قَالَ: إِذَا دَخَلَ الرَّجُلُ بَيْتَهُ، اسْتُحِبَّ لَهُ أَنْ يَتَنَحْنَحَ، أَوْ يُحَرِّكَ نَعْلَيْهِ.

وَلِهَذَا جَاءَ فِي الصَّحِيحِ، عَنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ: أَنَّهُ نَهَى أَنْ يَطْرُقَ الرَّجُلُ أهلَه طُروقًا -وَفِي رِوَايَة: لَيْلًا يَتَخوَّنهم .

وَفِي الْحَدِيثِ الْآخَرِ: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ قَدِمَ الْمَدِينَةَ نَهَارًا، فَأَنَاخَ بِظَاهِرِهَا، وَقَالَ: "انْتَظِرُوا حَتَّى تَدْخُلَ عَشَاءٌ -يَعْنِي: آخِرَ النَّهَارِ -حَتَّى تَمْتَشِطَ الشَّعثَة وَتَسْتَحِدَّ المُغَيبة" .

وَقَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ: حدَّثنا أَبِي، حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو بَكْرِ بْنُ أَبِي شَيْبَةَ، حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ سُلَيْمَانَ، عَنْ وَاصِلِ بْنِ السَّائِبِ، حدَّثني أَبُو سَوْرة ابْنِ أَخِي أَبِي أَيُّوبَ، عَنْ أَبِي أَيُّوبَ قَالَ: قُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، هَذَا السَّلَامُ، فَمَا الِاسْتِئْنَاسُ؟ قَالَ: "يَتَكَلَّمُ الرَّجُلُ بِتَسْبِيحَةٍ وَتَكْبِيرَةٍ وَتَحْمِيدَةٍ، وَيَتَنَحْنَحُ فَيؤذنُ أَهْلَ الْبَيْتِ". هَذَا حَدِيثٌ غَرِيبٌ .

وَقَالَ قَتَادَةُ فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿حَتَّى تَسْتَأْنِسُوا﴾ قَالَ: هُوَ الِاسْتِئْذَانُ. [قَالَ: وَكَانَ يُقَالُ: الِاسْتِئْذَانُ] ثَلَاثٌ، فَمَنْ لَمْ يُؤْذَنْ لَهُ فِيهِنَّ، فَلْيَرْجِعْ. أَمَّا الْأُولَى: فَلْيُسْمِعِ الْحَيَّ، وَأَمَّا الثَّانِيَةُ: فَلْيَأْخُذُوا حِذْرَهُمْ، وَأَمَّا الثَّالِثَةُ: فَإِنْ شَاءُوا أَذِنُوا وَإِنْ شَاءُوا رَدّوا. وَلَا تَقِفَنَّ عَلَى بَابِ قَوْمٍ رَدُّوكَ عَنْ بَابِهِمْ؛ فَإِنَّ لِلنَّاسِ حَاجَاتٍ وَلَهُمْ أَشْغَالٌ، وَاللَّهُ أَوْلَى بِالْعُذْرِ.

وَقَالَ مُقَاتِلُ بْنُ حيَّان فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لَا تَدْخُلُوا بُيُوتًا غَيْرَ بُيُوتِكُمْ حَتَّى تَسْتَأْنِسُوا وَتُسَلِّمُوا عَلَى أَهْلِهَا﴾ كَانَ الرَّجُلُ فِي الْجَاهِلِيَّةِ إِذَا لَقِيَ صَاحِبَهُ، لَا يُسَلِّمُ عَلَيْهِ، وَيَقُولُ: حُيِّيتَ صَبَاحًا وَحُيِّيتَ مَسَاءً، وَكَانَ ذَلِكَ تَحِيَّةَ الْقَوْمِ بَيْنَهُمْ. وَكَانَ أَحَدُهُمْ يَنْطَلِقُ إِلَى صَاحِبِهِ فَلَا يَسْتَأْذِنُ حَتَّى يَقْتَحِمَ، وَيَقُولَ: "قَدْ دخلتُ". فَيَشُقُّ ذَلِكَ عَلَى الرَّجُلِ، وَلَعَلَّهُ يَكُونُ مَعَ أَهْلِهِ، فغَيَّر اللَّهُ ذَلِكَ كُلَّهُ، فِي سَتْرٍ وَعِفَّةِ، وَجَعَلَهُ نَقْيًّا نَزِهًا مِنَ الدَّنَسِ وَالْقَذِرِ والدرَن، فَقَالَ: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لَا تَدْخُلُوا بُيُوتًا غَيْرَ بُيُوتِكُمْ حَتَّى تَسْتَأْنِسُوا وَتُسَلِّمُوا عَلَى أَهْلِهَا﴾ .

وَهَذَا الَّذِي قَالَهُ مُقَاتِلٌ حَسَنٌ؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ: ﴿ذَلِكُمْ خَيْرٌ لَكُمْ﴾ يَعْنِي: الِاسْتِئْذَانُ خَيْرٌ لَكُمْ، بِمَعْنَى: هُوَ خَيْرٌ لِلطَّرَفَيْنِ : لِلْمُسْتَأْذِنِ وَلِأَهْلِ الْبَيْتِ، ﴿. لَعَلَّكُمْ تَذَكَّرُونَ﴾ .

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿فَإِنْ لَمْ تَجِدُوا فِيهَا أَحَدًا فَلا تَدْخُلُوهَا حَتَّى يُؤْذَنَ لَكُمْ﴾ ، وَذَلِكَ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنَ التَّصَرُّفِ فِي مِلْكِ الْغَيْرِ بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِهِ، فَإِنْ شَاءَ أَذِنَ، وَإِنْ شَاءَ لَمْ يَأْذَنْ ﴿وَإِنْ قِيلَ لَكُمُ ارْجِعُوا فَارْجِعُوا هُوَ أَزْكَى لَكُمْ﴾ أَيْ: إِذَا رَدُّوكم مِنَ الْبَابِ قَبْلَ الْإِذْنِ أَوْ بَعْدَهُ ﴿فَارْجِعُوا هُوَ أَزْكَى لَكُمْ﴾ أَيْ: رُجُوعُكُمْ أَزْكَى لَكُمْ وَأَطْهَرُ ﴿وَاللهُ بِمَا تَعْملُونَ عَلِيم﴾ .

وَقَالَ قَتَادَةُ: قَالَ بَعْضُ الْمُهَاجِرِينَ: لَقَدْ طلبتُ عُمْرِي كلَّه هَذِهِ الْآيَةَ فَمَا أَدْرَكْتُهَا: أَنْ أستأذنَ عَلَى بَعْضِ إِخْوَانِي، فَيَقُولُ لِي: "ارْجِعْ"، فَأَرْجِعُ وَأَنَا مُغْتَبِطٌ [لِقَوْلِهِ] ، ﴿وَإِنْ قِيلَ لَكُمُ ارْجِعُوا فَارْجِعُوا هُوَ أَزْكَى لَكُمْ وَاللَّهُ بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ عَلِيمٌ﴾ .

وَقَالَ سَعِيدُ بْنُ جُبَيْرٍ: ﴿وَإِنْ قِيلَ لَكُمُ ارْجِعُوا فَارْجِعُوا﴾ أَيْ: لَا تَقِفُوا عَلَى أَبْوَابِ النَّاسِ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿لَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ جُنَاحٌ أَنْ تَدْخُلُوا بُيُوتًا غَيْرَ مَسْكُونَةٍ فِيهَا مَتَاعٌ لَكُمْ وَاللَّهُ يَعْلَمُ مَا تُبْدُونَ وَمَا تَكْتُمُونَ﴾ هَذِهِ الْآيَةُ الْكَرِيمَةُ أخصُّ مِنَ الَّتِي قَبْلَهَا، وَذَلِكَ أَنَّهَا تَقْتَضِي جَوَازَ الدُّخُولِ إِلَى الْبُيُوتِ الَّتِي لَيْسَ فِيهَا أَحَدٌ، إِذَا كَانَ لَهُ فِيهَا مَتَاعٌ، بِغَيْرِ إِذْنٍ، كَالْبَيْتِ الْمُعَدِّ لِلضَّيْفِ، إِذَا أُذِنَ لَهُ فِيهِ أَوَّلَ مَرَّةٍ، كَفَى.

قَالَ ابْنُ جُرَيْجٍ: قَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ: ﴿لَا تَدْخُلُوا بُيُوتًا غَيْرَ بُيُوتِكُمْ﴾ ، ثُمَّ نَسَخَ وَاسْتَثْنَى فَقَالَ ﴿لَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ جُنَاحٌ أَنْ تَدْخُلُوا بُيُوتًا غَيْرَ مَسْكُونَةٍ فِيهَا مَتَاعٌ لَكُمْ﴾ : وَكَذَا رُوِيَ عَنْ عِكْرِمَةَ، وَالْحَسَنِ الْبَصْرِيِّ.

وَقَالَ آخَرُونَ: هِيَ بُيُوتُ التُّجَّارِ، كَالْخَانَاتِ وَمَنَازِلِ الْأَسْفَارِ، وَبُيُوتِ مَكَّةَ، وَغَيْرِ ذَلِكَ. وَاخْتَارَ ذَلِكَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ، وَحَكَاهُ، عَنْ جَمَاعَةٍ. وَالْأَوَّلُ أَظْهَرُ، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

وَقَالَ مَالِكٌ عَنْ زَيْدِ بْنِ أَسْلَمَ: هِيَ بُيُوتُ الشَّعر.

---

## 24:30 — verse 30

### Translation

This is a command from God, exalted is He, to His believing servants that they lower their gaze from what He has forbidden them, so that they look only at what He has permitted them to look at, and that they restrain their eyes from forbidden things. If it happens that the gaze falls upon something forbidden without intention, one must turn one's gaze away from it quickly, as Muslim reported in his Sahih, from the hadith of Yunus ibn Ubayd, from Amr ibn Sa'id, from Abu Zur'ah ibn Amr ibn Jarir, from his grandfather Jarir ibn Abdullah al-Bajali, may God be pleased with him, who said: I asked the Prophet ﷺ about the sudden glance, and he commanded me to turn my gaze away.

Imam Ahmad likewise reported it, from Hushaym, from Yunus ibn Ubayd, with the same chain. Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and al-Nasa'i also reported it from his hadith. Al-Tirmidhi said: hasan sahih (good and authentic). In a version reported by some of them, he said: "Cast your gaze down," meaning: look at the ground. But "turning away" is more general, for it may be toward the ground or toward another direction. God knows best.

Abu Dawud said: [chain] Isma'il ibn Musa al-Fazari told us, Sharik told us, from Abu Rabi'ah al-Iyadi, from Abdullah ibn Buraydah, from his father, who said: The Messenger of God ﷺ said to Ali: "O Ali, do not let one glance follow another, for the first one is permitted to you but not the second."

Al-Tirmidhi also reported it from the hadith of Sharik, and said: gharib (singular), we know it only from his hadith.

In the Sahih, from Abu Sa'id, who said: The Messenger of God ﷺ said: "Beware of sitting on the roadsides." They said: O Messenger of God, we cannot avoid our gatherings in which we converse. The Messenger of God ﷺ said: "If you refuse, then give the road its due." They said: What is the due of the road, O Messenger of God? He said: "Lowering the gaze, refraining from causing harm, returning the greeting, enjoining what is right, and forbidding what is wrong."

Abu al-Qasim al-Baghawi said: [chain] Talut ibn Abbad told us, Fadl ibn Jubayr told us: I heard Abu Umamah say: I heard the Messenger of God ﷺ say: "Guarantee me six things and I will guarantee you Paradise: when one of you speaks, let him not lie; when he is entrusted with something, let him not betray it; when he makes a promise, let him not break it. And lower your gazes, restrain your hands, and guard your private parts."

In Sahih al-Bukhari: "Whoever guarantees me what is between his two jaws and what is between his two legs, I guarantee him Paradise."

Abd al-Razzaq said: Ma'mar informed us, from Ayyub, from Ibn Sirin, from Ubaydah, who said: Whatever God is disobeyed by is a major sin. He mentioned both extremes when He said: {Tell the believing men to lower their gaze}.

Since looking is a provocation leading to the corruption of the heart, as some of the salaf (early generations) said: "The gaze is a poisoned arrow to the heart," God therefore commanded the guarding of the private parts just as He commanded the guarding of the eyes, which are the incitements to that. He said: {Tell the believing men to lower their gaze and guard their private parts}. Guarding the private part is sometimes by preventing it from fornication, as He said: {And those who guard their private parts, except from their wives or those whom their right hands possess, for indeed they are not to be blamed} [al-Ma'arij: 29-30]. And sometimes it is by guarding it from being looked at, as has come in the hadith in the Musnad of Ahmad and the Sunan: "Guard your private part, except from your wife or what your right hand possesses."

{That is purer for them}, meaning: purer for their hearts and cleaner for their religion, as it has been said: "Whoever guards his gaze, God will bequeath him a light in his insight." And it is also narrated: "in his heart."

Imam Ahmad said: [chain] Attab told us, Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak told us, Yahya ibn Ayyub informed us, from Ubaydullah ibn Zahr, from Ali ibn Yazid, from al-Qasim, from Abu Umamah, may God be pleased with him, from the Prophet ﷺ, who said: "There is no Muslim who looks at the beauty of a woman [for the first time] and then lowers his gaze, except that God will replace it for him with an act of worship whose sweetness he will find."

This has also been reported as marfu' (elevated to the Prophet) from Ibn Umar, Hudhayfah, and A'ishah, may God be pleased with them, but there is weakness in its chain, though it falls under encouragement to good, and such matters are treated leniently.

In al-Tabarani, through the route of Ubaydullah ibn Zahr, from Ali ibn Yazid, from al-Qasim, from Abu Umamah, marfu': "You will surely lower your gazes, and you will surely guard your private parts, and you will surely keep your faces upright, or your faces will be darkened."

Al-Tabarani said: [chain] Ahmad ibn Zuhayr al-Tustari told us: We read to Muhammad ibn Hafs ibn Umar al-Darir al-Muqri, Yahya ibn Abi Bukayr told us, Hurayn ibn Sufyan told us, from Abd al-Rahman ibn Ishaq, from al-Qasim ibn Abd al-Rahman, from his father, from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, may God be pleased with him, who said: The Messenger of God ﷺ said: "Indeed the gaze is one of the poisoned arrows of Iblis. Whoever abandons it out of fear of Me, I will replace it for him with faith whose sweetness he will find in his heart."

His saying: {Indeed God is well acquainted with what they do}, as He, exalted is He, said: {He knows the treachery of the eyes and what the breasts conceal} [Ghafir: 19].

In the Sahih, from Abu Hurayrah, may God be pleased with him, who said: The Messenger of God ﷺ said: "It has been decreed for the son of Adam his share of fornication, which he will inevitably attain. The fornication of the eyes is the look, the fornication of the tongue is the speech, the fornication of the ears is the listening, the fornication of the hands is the grasping, the fornication of the feet is the walking, and the heart desires and wishes, and the private part confirms that or denies it."

Al-Bukhari reported it as a mu'allaq (suspended report) and Muslim reported it as musnad (connected) through another route, with wording similar to what has preceded.

Many of the salaf said: they used to forbid a man from fixing his gaze upon a beardless youth. Many of the leading Sufis were strict about this, and a group of the people of knowledge prohibited it, on account of the temptation it involves, and others were extremely strict about it indeed.

Ibn Abi al-Dunya said: [chain] Abu Sa'id al-Madani told us, Umar ibn Sahl al-Mazini told us, Umar ibn Muhammad ibn Suhban told me, Safwan ibn Sulaym told me, from Abu Hurayrah, may God be pleased with him, who said: The Messenger of God ﷺ said: "Every eye will be weeping on the Day of Resurrection, except an eye that lowered itself from what God has forbidden, and an eye that stayed awake in the way of God, and an eye from which there comes forth something like the head of a fly, out of fear of God, mighty and majestic is He."

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

هَذَا أَمْرٌ مِنَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى لِعِبَادِهِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ أَنْ يَغُضُّوا مِنْ أَبْصَارِهِمْ عَمَّا حَرَّمَ عَلَيْهِمْ، فَلَا يَنْظُرُوا إِلَّا إِلَى مَا أَبَاحَ لَهُمُ النَّظَرَ إِلَيْهِ ، وَأَنْ يَغُضُّوا أَبْصَارَهُمْ عَنِ الْمَحَارِمِ، فَإِنِ اتَّفَقَ أَنْ وَقَعَ الْبَصَرُ عَلَى مُحرَّم مِنْ غَيْرِ قَصْدٍ، فَلْيَصْرِفْ بَصَرَهُ عَنْهُ سَرِيعًا، كَمَا رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ فِي صَحِيحِهِ، مِنْ حَدِيثِ يُونُسَ بْنِ عُبَيد، عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ سَعِيدٍ، عَنْ أَبِي زُرْعَة بْنِ عَمْرِو بْنِ جَرِيرٍ، عَنْ جَدِّهِ جَرِيرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ الْبَجَلِيُّ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، قَالَ: سَأَلْتُ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ، عَنْ نَظْرَةِ الْفَجْأَةِ، فَأَمَرَنِي أَنْ أصرفَ بَصَري.
